Basketball and Football Referees

Shanghai Sports Referees Association Appointed

Peng Sanmei Acts as Chairman of Basketball Competition

The Shanghai Sports Referees Association was appointed by letter to serve as football and basketball referees. Xu Zhendong, Chairman of the Basketball Committee, was unable to attend due to other commitments and requested Peng Sanmei to act as his proxy.

Eligibility of Participating Athletes

All students of secondary schools and above in this city, as well as citizens, except those who are employed in sports, are eligible to participate. Athletes participating in track and field all-around, swimming, tennis, and national martial arts are counted as individuals. Teams participating in football, basketball, and baseball are counted as units.

Types of Tournament Championships

The types of tournament championships will follow the National Games regulations, totaling seventeen categories.

A. Men's Division

Zi. Field Event Championship, Chou. Track Event Championship, Yin. All-Around Championship, Mao. Swimming Championship, Chen. Football Championship, Si. Basketball Championship, Wu. Tennis Championship, Wei. Volleyball Championship, Shen. Baseball Championship

B. Women's Division

Zi. Track and Field Championship, Chou. Swimming Championship, Yin. Basketball Championship, Mao. Tennis Championship, Chen. Volleyball Championship

C. National Martial Arts Division

Zi. Wrestling Championship, Chou. Fencing Championship, Yin. Grappling Championship. National Martial Arts Championships are divided into men's and women's groups, but the events are the same.

Method for Athletes to Win Championships

For field events, track events, all-around sports, and swimming, the championship goes to the one with the most points. If two or more athletes score the same number of points, the championship goes to the one with more first-place finishes. If the number of first-place finishes is equal, the winner is determined by the number of second-place finishes, and so on. The winner of the final in ball games wins the championship.

Today's Predictions for Men's and Women's Track and Field Preliminary and Final Rounds

Men's Finals

▲Discus Throw: Shanghai is lagging behind in the progress of various track and field sports. Only the discus throw event has progressed very slowly. Each time, in the sports meeting, the progress has not been good. After investigating, although there are thirteen people participating in the finals of the discus throw event, which is the first final of today's city sports meeting, there is a lack of good generals. According to past results, Wang Jihuai, Chen Baoqiu, Cao Yu, Xie Quanhe, and Luo Chuanxian, and Fu Hongxing are the best performers. However, Wang Jihuai injured the back of his foot with running shoe nails during practice at Jinan University, and it has been festering for a long time, making it difficult for him to walk for almost two weeks. Although he has fully recovered, he has been lacking in practice for a long time, and his results will inevitably be slightly inferior. Chen Baoqiu's performance has been good and bad, sometimes throwing 34 or 35 meters, sometimes throwing around 30 meters. This is probably due to a lack of experience. Recently, it has been said that Mr. Chen has been suffering from malaria for more than a day, so his energy has been greatly reduced. It is still questionable whether he can participate today. The other four, Cao, Xie, Luo, and Fu, have similar results. Cao and Xie may be able to compete for positions because they are more experienced. However, it has been said that Mr. Luo has been progressing very quickly recently.

▲Long Jump: Among the forty-three people, those competing for the final right are none other than Wang Jihuai, Hao Chunde, Chen Gongyu, Zhong Lianji, Li Lin, and Wu Jinqi. Wang Jihuai and Lang Chunde are more likely to win the championship. However, Wang Jihuai has just recovered from a foot injury. Although he may be able to win the championship, it is expected that he will not be able to achieve the results he jumped in the Jiangda Sports Meeting in the first half of the year. Chen and Zhong's performance in competing for positions will also be considerable and will not be too far behind Wang and Lang. Mr. Li can often jump to about 6.20 meters, but due to his physique, it is difficult for him to have an amazing performance. Mr. Wu has excellent arch elasticity, but he is prone to muscle strain when long jumping. According to the reporter's opinion, Mr. Wu can give up long jumping and concentrate on high jumping to win the championship. I wonder what Mr. Wu thinks.

▲High Jump: There are also as many as twenty-five people participating in the high jump, but it is expected that at least three-fifths of them will be eliminated before 1.60 meters. The final winners will be Wu Jinqi, Li Lin, and Gu Yu. Wu and Li both use the Horahine jumping method. Since the new rules were adopted, both have felt quite disadvantaged. Comparing the two, Mr. Li is even more disadvantaged. Mr. Gu's jumping method is excellent, but due to his height, it is extremely difficult for him to make further progress. Wu Jinqi accompanied the Jiangnan team on its northern expedition during the summer vacation. When competing against Luhe in Beiping, it was said that he was only one level behind Li Junzhong when competing for first place, and was ranked second. On that day, Mr. Li's score was 1.84 meters. It is estimated that Mr. Wu's score is at least 1.80 meters. If so, Mr. Wu seems more confident in winning the high jump championship.

Women's Finals

▲ Long Jump

Yesterday, in the registry of the Bureau of Education, a check of the entire list of female applicants revealed that two-thirds were students from women's sports schools. However, statistically, students from women's sports schools account for less than one-tenth of the total number of female athletes in Shanghai's middle and higher schools. This shows the lack of popularity of women's sports in other schools, which is a sign of the depression of women's sports in the city. As for the scores in various women's track and field events, it is difficult to predict at this early stage, and upsets are very likely. Based on past women's long jump results in Shanghai, Ms. Zhang Ping, Qian Hangsu, and Chen Yunqing are the most promising. However, the reporter hopes that a new player with amazing results will defeat the old players in today's city games and create a new record. It is hoped that this kind of news will be heard repeatedly in this sports meet.

▲ High Jump

The women's high jump is the most immature aspect of women's sports. Not to mention the performance, even the jumping posture is not correct in one out of a hundred attempts. Having traveled all over Shanghai, I have not seen a beautiful high jump posture. However, based on the high jump results of female students in secondary schools in the first half of the year, Ms. Zhang Baojin, Yang Zhiren, and Sun Xiaoxia should be considered the best. Because Ms. Zhang, Yang, and Sun have won positions, and Ms. Zhang even created a new record of 1.26 meters in the immature category. However, this situation can easily change. What kind of situation will be created in today's game is beyond the reporter's intelligence to predict. I only hope that the ladies will strive to compete. Victory or defeat is not important, but progress in performance is the most important.

Men's Preliminaries

▲ 100-Meter Preliminary

Everyone in Shanghai who emphasizes the short sprint highlights Zhong Liantai, Hao Chunde, Gu Zaiping, Zhou Ende, Lin Guangyu, and He Debao. It is undoubtedly true that these six gentlemen are listed at the top of the six groups in today's preliminary rounds. However, Mr. Lin Guangxing of Shanghai College suffered from diarrhea a few days ago. Although he gradually recovered yesterday, his muscles have become thin and his spirit is weak. Yesterday, the reporter saw Mr. Peng Sanmei, the director of physical education at Shanghai College, and asked for his opinion. According to him, he plans to let him participate in the preliminary round to see how the results of the first preliminary round will be and then make a decision based on the situation. The reporter recalled the previous Jiangda Games, when Wang Jihuai of Guanghua was in the same situation as Mr. Lin. At that time, he was persuaded to value his health and not to force himself to participate. Unexpectedly, Mr. Wang won three championships in the two-day games, winning the first place in the long jump, triple jump, and javelin events. The javelin also set a new record for Jiangda. Those who watched the game in the arena laughed and said, "Wang Jihuai was sick but bravely challenged An Dianbao, and one shot broke the old record." The reporter hopes that Mr. Lin can be like Mr. Wang today, becoming a miraculous Taibao despite his illness.

▲ 200-Meter Preliminary

The four great generals, Zhong, Hao, Gu, and Zhou, should be able to make a splash in the 200-meter preliminary round. Mr. Lin Guangxing could have competed with the four great generals, but after the diarrhea, it is feared that it will be difficult to compete for victory. However, there is a rising star, Mr. Zeng Rongzhong of Jinan, who can be considered a strong enemy of the four. Let us wait and see.

▲ 400-Meter Preliminary

At the previous Wan Guo Games, the Chinese team members of the 1600-meter relay, Zeng Rongzhong, He Debao, Su Zuqing, and Wang Jianwu, can control the situation in the four preliminary rounds. Among them, Mr. Wang Jianwu is thirty-seven years old, which is older, but his spirit is still undiminished from his heyday (fifteen years ago) at the Jiangsu Provincial Games. Moreover, his results are also improving with age. However, although he has been practicing diligently this year, his results are not as good as last year. It is thought that the relationship between age and energy is powerless.

▲ 800-Meter Preliminary

As many as fifty-seven people have joined the 800-meter race. Some say that a quarter of them will not show up for the race. Among those who show up, half will not be able to run the entire distance. Therefore, this preliminary round is rarely exciting. In terms of results, Chen Xingpei in the first group and Qiu Lingru in the second group are better, and the rest are average.

▲ 1500-Meter Preliminary

Among the sixty-three contestants, the reporter dares to say that at least some of them are speculative. Their purpose is to obtain an athlete's badge by joining the competition, not to improve their skills. Whether this is the case remains to be confirmed by roll call in today's preliminary round. The reporter speculates on their psychology. Other sports are not easy to fake, but only middle-distance running, such as the 1500 meters and 10,000 meters, etc., in the first and second laps, anyone can follow. When the original strength cannot continue, they will withdraw halfway, or claim to have a stomachache, or claim to have a foot pain. All kinds of strange phenomena are everywhere. At this point, they think that the responsibility of joining the sports meet is over. They put on their clothes, wear their badges, and run around, causing such goods to be everywhere. In the past, there have also been Boy Scouts who came forward to intervene. They all said that they were athletes. The habit has been like this for a long time. However, today's city athletes will not have to pay registration fees, which will make it even worse. Although this is said, I hope that those who join the 1500-meter race will not be included in the reporter's preliminary predictions. Everyone can come to the competition and run the entire distance. The 1500 meters is one of the most lacking talents in Shanghai. The best result is finally around 4 minutes and 30 seconds, which is far from the comparison with Liaoning. In the four groups of races, Zhang Hugen is the most confident in the first group, Zhou Bin is very hopeful in the second group, Chen Xingpei will definitely be selected in the third group, and Qiu Lingru can control the victory in the fourth group. However, the reporter deeply hopes that new talents will appear in each group and not let the old generals occupy the beauty for a long time.

▲ Middle and High Hurdles Preliminary

Hurdling is not easy, so not many people join the competition. There are only fifteen people in the high hurdles and only seventeen people in the middle hurdles. Among the high hurdles, Cao Yu's results are the best, followed by Tao Yingjie, Zhou Shaowen, and Chen Buzhang. Mr. Chen Guoquan, who won the first place in the high hurdles at the Wan Guo Games in the spring, has not joined this time, for some reason. Among the middle hurdles, Tao Yingjie is the best, followed by Sun Huipei and Chen Buzhang. Chen Baoqiu may not be able to participate in this sport due to illness. Last night, it was also learned that Mr. Tao Yingjie, the holder of the middle hurdles record, has dampness in his feet, and I don't know if it will affect the results.

Women's Preliminary

▲ 50-Meter Preliminary

Ms. Zhang Pingxian, Sheng Bi, Ma Yufang, and Situ Wei are the most promising to win the championship in the preliminary rounds of each group.

▲ 100-Meter Preliminary

Zhang Pingxian, Zhang Jingfang, Sheng Bi, Situ Wei, Zhu Wencheng, Pan Huilin, and others compete for the first place in each group. Among them, Ms. Zhang Pingxian's results should be the best.

▲ 200-Meter Preliminary

Ms. Liu Jingfang is the best in the 200 meters, but whether she can maintain her previous results this year is still a question, because the age of women is related to sports. In addition, Situ Wei, Zhu Wencheng, Ma Yufang, Luo Huilin, and others are also good.

▲ Low Hurdles Preliminary

This sport is being pioneered in Shanghai this time and has not been competed before, so the results are still unknown.

No Leave for Sports

The Municipal Bureau of Education believes that the physical education teachers of various schools have enthusiastically supported and served at this conference, and the students of various schools have actively participated, forming a grand event. Yesterday, they sent letters to various schools, stating that all school staff members who serve at the conference and students who participate in the competition can be allowed to attend the conference on a daily basis without being marked absent, in order to emphasize sports.

Registration deadline changed to 5:00 PM today

Yesterday, Mayor Zhang mentioned this matter at the municipal meeting. The mayor's secretary, councillors, and bureau chiefs were happy to participate in order to promote it. The originally scheduled competition schedule may change accordingly. However, the competition dates are determined to be on the 19th and 20th.

At 4:00 PM at the French Chamber of Commerce

Earthquake Relief Basketball Finale Jinan Wins Qingguang

37 to 34

The last earthquake relief basketball game was held last night, with Jinan winning Qingguang 37 to 34. Jinan scored consecutively in the last ten minutes, driving up. Referee Qian Yiqin, in conjunction with today's report, collected 30 tickets last night.

Local News

City Boy Scouts to Collect Donations Along the Way Today

Donation scope··· All sectors of the Chinese Concession

Divided areas··· Total of thirty districts

Number of participants · Total of thirty-two districts

The Shanghai Boy Scout Flood Relief Donation Committee has decided to hold a roadside fundraising campaign today, from 6:00 am to 12:00 pm. The following are the detailed circumstances.

▲ List of Staff

Donation General Captain Tong Xingbai, Deputy General Captains Gu Zheng Lai · Wang Yiqiao, Inspectors Dai Qi Liu · Jin Xing · Chen Zizhen · Feng Zhenwei · Cai Jingshen · Zhou Guoji · Zhao Weizu, District Captains, District 1 Huang Shan, District 2 Zhang Xunfang, District 3 Zhu Chongde, District 4 Ye Chunnian, District 5 Chen Zhenxiang, District 6 Wang Wenhua, District 7 Jiang Yinsheng, District 8 Zheng Runsang, District 9 Luo Lie, District 10 Li Jinfang, District 11 Cao Yuncheng, District 12 Cao Yuncheng, District 13 Yin Daozhong, District 14 Yu Kuiyuan, District 15 Chen Yinzhang, District 16 Ni Jia　, District 17 Gu Zhenxian, District 18 Qu Yue, District 19 Xi Youchang, District 20 Tang Jirui, District 21 Huang Yangren, District 22 Hua Mingsheng, District 23 Sun Yixin, District 24 Huang Shengbai, District 25 Jiang Peng, District 26 Cai Xianmin, District 27 Zou Yinlu, District 28 Zhou Fagao, District 29 Huang Songcao, District 30 Song Derun,

▲ Donation Instructions

(1) The donation date is set from 6:00 am to 12:00 pm on September 12. (2) All service staff and Boy Scouts participating in the donation must be neatly dressed, speak kindly, and show the Boy Scout spirit at all times and places. If someone is unwilling to donate, do not speak harshly to them, but still treat them with courtesy. (3) When donating, you must do your best to collect donations within the designated area, and do not go outside the area to avoid overlapping with other groups. (4) The donations should be personally put into the donation box by the donors. (5) The donation box must be carefully kept and must not be opened without authorization. (6) All expenses on the day of the donation will be borne by the participants themselves to save expenses. (7) Within the designated area, if there are hotels, amusement parks, teahouses, restaurants, as well as other foreign firms, companies, large and small official residences, etc., you can go to solicit donations, but you must not violate their order. (8) All actions during the donation should be cautious to avoid accidents. (9) You must absolutely obey the command of the captain during the donation. (10) For donations of one yuan or more, a yellow thank-you note will be given. For donations of two corners or more, a white thank-you note will be given. If the thank-you notes are used up, you can borrow them from other team members who have not used them up, or explain to the donors, and do not stop donating. (11) After the donation is completed, send the donation box to the Mu'er Hall in the Racecourse on Sanma Road, and register your name, number, and donation box. The association will give you a receipt as proof.

▲ Begging for Relief

Disasters have befallen our people, and the victims of this flood are all over more than ten provinces. The old and weak have been abandoned in ditches, and the strong and young are waiting to be fed. Anyone with a little kindness cannot help but save money and donate generously. Our Boy Scouts follow the spirit of helping others anytime and anywhere, hoping to save those victims from deep water and fire. Therefore, this association has been organized. I hope that people from all walks of life will not shirk their responsibility, donate generously, and gather a little to make a lot, and accumulate sand to form a tower. Donating one yuan means saving one more life. The Boy Scouts who are donating along the way are all wearing uniforms and have donation team badges to help them identify. In addition to inviting party and government agencies to open the box publicly at Mu'er Hall, Xizang Road, Hankou Road the next day to show caution, the donated relief money will be transferred to the flood relief committees in various provinces for distribution. This announcement.

▲ Date of Opening the Box

The Boy Scout Group is scheduled to open the box at 10:00 am on the 13th of this month in the auditorium of Mu'er Hall on Xizang Road, and has sent letters to newspaper reporters and various agencies and groups to supervise the opening of the box to show solemnity.

Disaster Relief News from Various Provinces Yesterday

The National Government Disaster Relief Committee held a standing committee meeting yesterday

The National Government Flood Relief Committee held its first plenary meeting on the 9th and decided to add 12 standing committee members (a total of 17 members). Yesterday afternoon at 5:00 pm, it convened a standing committee meeting at Song Ziwen's residence on Bixun Road in the French Concession to discuss matters such as American wheat. Committee members Song Ziwen, Standing Committee members Zhu Qinglan, Zeng Hongpu, Liu Ruiheng, Yu Qiaqing, and foreign standing committee members Baker, Maxwell, Carney, and Funatsu, and others attended, totaling more than a dozen people. The discussion lasted for more than an hour, and it ended at 6:15 pm. As a result, it was decided to start shipping 30,000 tons this month, 60,000 tons next month (October), and 75,000 tons each month from November to February of next year, and 60,000 tons in March, totaling 450,000 tons.

▲ Allocation of Funds to Various Provinces

The funds that the National Government Flood Relief Committee discussed at the plenary meeting should be allocated to various provinces, including 400,000 yuan for Hubei, 300,000 yuan for northern Anhui, 300,000 yuan for Jiangsu, and 100,000 yuan each for Jiangxi, Hunan, and Henan. The Central Bank has remitted the above to the collection points in the above-mentioned areas yesterday.

▲ Committee Member Zhu Receives Report

National Government Flood Relief Committee General Zhu Cijian, Yangqing's two telegrams, have been received. The relief funds have been received. The burial has been entrusted to the Wuhu Flood Relief Association to form a team, which will depart immediately to implement. The urgent relief of Langxi's five counties has been entrusted to the Wanzi Association to go separately to work with the local area to conduct a thorough investigation. Grain seeds will be reported separately after verification. Zhang Rujun kowtows and steams.

▲ Do Not Accept Various Proprietary Medicines

The Health and Epidemic Prevention Group of the National Government Flood Relief Committee issued the following opinions on donated medicines: Many Chinese and foreign pharmaceutical companies and philanthropists have donated medical supplies and various medicines to the Health and Epidemic Prevention Group, which has greatly helped the health and epidemic prevention work in the disaster area. However, there are occasional donations of proprietary medicines, which are sometimes not entirely suitable for the needs of the disaster area, which may be a waste of the donor's good intentions. The group has issued statements in Chinese and foreign newspapers, welcoming donations of medicines listed in the pharmacopoeias of various countries. As for various proprietary medicines, we regret that we cannot accept them. If you have any questions about donating medicines, you can also contact the Health and Epidemic Prevention Group of the Flood Relief Committee on Jiujiang Road at any time to facilitate the matter.

Jiangsu Flood Relief Association Executive Committee Meeting

The Jiangsu Flood Relief Association held its first executive committee meeting at the Renji Hall on Sixth Avenue yesterday at 4 PM. Attendees included committee members Huang Hanzhi, Wang Binyan, Weng Yinchu, Wen Lanting, Shi Liangcai, Hu Bijian, Ha Shaofu, Gu Xinyi, Wu Yunbao, Qin Runqing, Qin Yanqi, Chen Guangfu, Cheng Jingsheng, Huang Ruisheng, Sun Bowen, Niu Tisheng, Wang Peiyuan, Lu Shaoliu, Zhou Weishi, Zheng Zhongshan, Xi Yunsheng, Ni Wenqing, Zhu Xiechen, Wang Xiaolai, Ye Fuxiao, Xu Qianlin, and Wang Yiting. Present as observers were Zhu Ganchen, Liang Ruiting, and Xie Yaosan. Wang Yiting chaired the meeting, with Xiao Zhantong as the recording secretary.

(Reported Matters)

(1) 361 telegrams received from various counties reporting disasters and requesting relief.

(2) The Standing Committee reported on the extension of invitations to directors of various counties to handle urgent relief efforts.

(3) Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng personally went to the disaster areas in northern Jiangsu to establish offices and organize emergency relief for the victims, reporting on the situation.

(4) The Standing Committee reported on the investigations of disaster areas by investigators from various counties.

(5) The Economic Committee of the Standing Committee reported on the amounts of relief funds already allocated to various counties.

(6) The Standing Committee reported on the amount of rice and flour purchased and distributed to the disaster areas.

(7) The Standing Committee reported that Director Cao, from among the donors, had resigned, and the resolution to appoint Director Guo Yuye in his place to handle matters had been passed.

(8) The Standing Committee reported that the office’s affairs were busy and complex. It was publicly agreed to reorganize the methods as follows:

(A) Establish a sign-in book, from 9 AM to 7 PM, with extensions possible in special circumstances.

(B) Personnel for receiving, dispatching, and managing documents should move to the Association's premises.

(C) Submissions should be signed or stamped with a seal.

(D) Incoming documents should be reviewed twice daily, at 11 AM and 4 PM.

(E) Hire additional secretaries.

(F) Assign personnel to handle thank-you advertisements in newspapers and printing matters.

(G) Assign proofreaders and translators of telegrams.

(H) Public relations matters should be handled concurrently by the review division.

(I) Hire additional transportation personnel for expediency.

(J) The accounting and general affairs divisions should expedite the creation of ten-day reports on relief funds and supplies.

(9) The Provincial Relief Commission sent a letter requesting the Association to divide the counties with the Zhenjiang Jiangbei Flood Relief Temporary Relief Association to handle urgent relief efforts.

(Matters for Discussion)

(1) Standing Committee member Wang Yiting, Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi, and Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng proposed to add Niu Tisheng, Sun Bowen, Leng Yuqiu, and Zhou Weishi as Standing Committee members of the Association. (Public Vote) Passed.

(2) Standing Committee member Wang Yiting, Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi, and Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng proposed to appoint a director and deputy director of the office. (Public Vote) Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng was appointed as Director, and Executive Committee member Lu Shaoliu was appointed as Deputy Director.

(3) Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng and Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi proposed to add Yu Jiankui, Zhang Jinghan, and Liu Yunqing as relief directors. (Public Vote) Passed.

(4) Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi proposed whether the Association should hire an accountant. (Public Vote) Xu Yongzuo was requested to serve as the accountant.

(5) Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng proposed that the Zhenjiang, Yangzhou, Gaoyou, Sishui, and Bao Ying Xinghua offices, as well as the Jiangpu and other sixteen county investigation and distribution bureaus, have repeatedly telegraphed requesting funds. How should the disbursements and allocations be handled? (Public Vote)

It should be handled by the Standing Committee and reported to the next executive committee meeting.

(6) Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng and Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi proposed how to provide relief to Gaochun, Nantong, and Dongting East Mountain, based on reported disaster conditions.

(7) Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi proposed how to urgently provide relief to Baoshan and Pingan, where the disaster situation is reportedly severe according to investigations. (Public Vote) Regarding cases six and seven, except for urgent relief to Gaochun, a letter should be sent to the Jiangbei Temporary Relief Association, requesting them to handle it expeditiously. The rest should be decided by the Standing Committee.

(8) Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng and Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi proposed adding the China & South Continent Bank branches to the Association's receiving locations, requesting ratification. (Public Vote) Passed.

(9) Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng proposed that the transportation of goods is currently extremely difficult. How should the Railway and Communications Ministries be consulted to grant special convenience? (Public Vote) Standing Committee member Niu Tisheng was requested to consult with the Railway and Communications Ministries first, and Executive Committee member Ni Wenqing was appointed as the head of the transportation division.

(10) Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi and Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng proposed that Executive Committee member Huang Boyu had requested to resign due to illness and should be persuaded to stay. (Public Vote) Persuade him to stay.

(11) Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi and Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng proposed that Mr. Weng Guoxun had written a letter stating that he had hundreds of pieces of calligraphy and paintings cherished by his relatives and friends, and he wished to donate them all for relief. (Public Vote) It was heard that there was talk in the city of forming a calligraphy and painting relief association for flood relief, and it will be incorporated into handling in the future.

(12) Standing Committee member Cheng Jingsheng and Standing Committee member Huang Hanzhi proposed that the disaster areas urgently need cotton clothing and that efforts should be made to solicit donations. Furthermore, livestock preservation is of utmost importance, and consultations should be held with various counties to establish livestock preservation centers. (Public Vote) The Standing Committee should discuss and determine a method.

During the meeting, Mr. Zhu Ganchen, representative of Jiangdu, reported on the work of the Association's Yangzhou office and the dire conditions in the townships east of Shaobo. The investigators have decided to prioritize remote areas for aid distribution. Standing Committee member Sun Bowen reported that he recently met with Mr. Huang Boyu and discussed borrowing American flour. Mr. Huang suggested transporting more wheat and less flour, as flour is prone to spoilage while wheat is more durable. This suggestion is insightful and should be noted. Standing Committee member Niu Tisheng reported that it is currently advisable to transport more wheat, as it is less likely to mold during the cold winter. More flour can be transported later. He will discuss this matter with the political authorities after returning to Beijing. Standing Committee member Xi Yunsheng reported on the disaster situation in Dongting Mountain. Mr. Ge Gongzhen, representative of Dongtai, reported on the disaster situation in Dongtai, expressing the urgent need for someone to go to Dongtai for relief and hoping that the breach can be closed as soon as possible, whether by new or old methods, and completed on schedule. In addition, he requested that officials and soldiers monitor the opening of the salt reclamation company's dikes for drainage.

(Amount of Relief Funds Received) As of today, a total of 228,283.965 yuan has been received, as well as 356.3 taels of silver, 408 small silver dollars, and 160 yuan worth of shares in the British American Tobacco Company.

(Amount of Relief Funds Disbursed) 18,500 yuan to the Provincial Office, 26,000 yuan to the Yangzhou Office, 10,000 yuan to the Post Office, 10,000 yuan to the Bao Office, 2,000 yuan to the Si Office, 20,000 yuan to the Xing Office, 1,500 yuan for urgent relief to Taicang, and 10,000 yuan for flour, totaling 98,000 yuan. More than 90,000 yuan is still waiting to be disbursed tomorrow. Also, 7,004 bags of flour, 40 boxes of biscuits, 600 pounds of bread, and 13,000 pieces of medicine, including wind-cold medicine, dysentery powder, holy water, quinine tablets, Jizhong water, Baodan pills, and Rendan pills, have been transported to the Zhenjiang, Yangzhou, Gaoyou, Si, and Xing offices.

Yangzhou Red Cross Society Relief Work

The Chinese Red Cross Society received a report from the Yangzhou branch yesterday stating that after the dike collapse in northern Jiangsu, the branch convened a temporary emergency meeting on the 28th to discuss measures. It was resolved that attendees would raise 2,000 catties of sesame cakes and Jingjiang cakes, 400 bottles of wind-cold medicine, and publicly appoint Guo Shaoting, Ruan Yuren, and Chen Peiqiu to lead six laborers to the disaster area by hired boat to distribute the supplies and bring along corpse retrieval equipment to prepare for salvaging bodies. They departed on the 29th. When the boat reached the Liuzha area, the water was turbulent, making it difficult to proceed. Although there were bodies, they were difficult to retrieve. Only the roofs of houses on land could be seen, and only the tops of trees were visible. Countless people were clinging to rooftops and treetops. The dry food and medicine brought were immediately distributed to the victims, and 46 elderly, weak, men, and women were rescued (the boat could not carry more) and transported back to Yangzhou, where they were sent to the Changsheng Temple reception center. Recognizing that the victims' most urgent need was dry food, flyers were widely distributed to solicit various food items. As a result, 3,000 catties of scorched rice, fried rice, large cakes, and Jiang cakes were raised. On the 31st, Ruan and others took them to Shaobo Yi Guangda, where there were many victims and a shortage of medicine and food. They respectfully requested immediate assistance to save the people. After receiving the report, the society telegraphed a reply stating that it would soon dispatch staff member Bao Kangning, along with doctors and nurses, to the disaster area to do their utmost to provide rescue.

Dire Situation in Disaster-Stricken Counties in Northern Jiangsu

The Emergency Relief Association has recently received numerous reports, letters, and telegrams from various counties in northern Jiangsu reporting the true extent of the disaster and appealing for relief. Excerpts are listed separately below:

▲ In Gaoyou, four breaches occurred in the dikes in the areas of Qigongdian, Yumatou, Miaoxiangkou, and Danggjunlou north of the city, one after another, within a distance of two li, suddenly forming three islands. The width of the breaches ranged from dozens of zhang to twenty or thirty zhang, with the largest breach at Danggjunlou, reaching one hundred fifty or sixty zhang. South of the city, the breach at Ershilipu was approximately ninety zhang, and the breach at Sanshilipu was approximately sixty zhang. The various dikes in the four rural areas of the county were successively breached, and floating corpses were everywhere.

▲ In Taixian, the accumulated water reached eight or nine chi. The southeastern townships, which typically grew dry crops, were completely submerged. The four districts downstream, which were the county's largest rice-producing areas, were simultaneously submerged, regardless of whether they were high or low-lying areas. After the opening of the Guihai Three Dams, the water depth outside the inclined embankment weirs in the downstream districts was six or seven chi. After just two days, the en-weir breaches occurred, and the water volume inside the weirs was equal to that outside the weirs. Not only was the late rice submerged, but it would also rot after prolonged exposure. Even most of the houses in the villages collapsed, leaving more than 100,000 people homeless. Many elderly, weak, women, and children were unable to escape and drifted away, and entire families drowned in various places.

▲ Since the collapse of Guazhou on August 27th, all 60,000 mu of fields and 5,000 houses in the entire weir were instantly submerged, and 100,000 lives were in imminent danger. The young and strong climbed to the tops of trees, while the elderly, weak, women, and children drowned in the water. Now that the autumn winds have suddenly risen and the cold pierces the skin, the people have no clothing or food and will freeze and starve to death.

▲ After the opening of the Jiangdu Gaoyou Three Dams, the lakes of Ailing, Xingsi, Luyang, and Qingdang rose simultaneously. Four or five out of ten weirs near the lake were submerged. After the Shaobo Dam collapsed on the 26th of last month, there were a dozen or more breaches along the embankment from Beibanchang to Zha Sanli. The nearby villages and towns downstream, such as Liuzhuang, Mazhuang, and Xiaojie, were completely washed away. The towns of Qishumiao, Yangjiazhuang, Zhenwumiao, Dinggou, Yong'an Qiaoshu, Chenjiadian Dingjiahuo, and Gaoqiao were completely submerged. The surrounding weir fields, such as the Huti Weir, Qishu Weir, Guangfeng Weir, Hefeng Weir, Tanjia Weir, Yangjiazhuang Weir, Zhenwumiao East Weir, and Zhang Shiliang Weir, were all completely submerged. The rice tips of the higher-lying fields without weirs in Shuixi Township, Zhoushu Township, Shao Xiannv Township, Yanshou Township, and Huanghua Township were completely submerged, and the rice ears of the shallow areas were slightly exposed above the water. A total of more than 20,000 mu of fields were submerged, affecting approximately 100,000 victims. The number of drowned people and animals could not be counted in the rush. Only floating corpses were seen drifting in the rivers and lakes, emitting a foul odor. Most of them flowed north to Gaoyou and Xinghua, and no one was retrieving or burying them.

The Jiangdu Seventh District Flood Relief Association issued an urgent notice stating that the district is east of Shaobo, directly facing the initial impact of the dike breaches at Liuzha and other places. The disaster situation is unbearable. Townships such as Qiaoshu, Dinggou, Dingjiahuo Yan, Huangshao, Shuizhou, and Hantang still have a water level of five or six chi. Victims are perched in trees and on rooftops, awaiting death. Because the area is remote, the relief supplies from major benefactors have mostly been transported to Shaobo for distribution, and the district has not received a drop of assistance. Although the major benefactors have donated a great deal of money, the victims in the district are still starving. In the future, if relief supplies are donated, please transport them from Xiannvmiao and Dahan directly to the Qiaoshu and Dinggou Flood Relief Offices for distribution to avoid being overlooked. Alternatively, please notify the Yangzhou Hotel in Nanliuxiang, and the association's Yangzhou office will send staff to distribute them in the disaster area. This notice was issued on September 7th.

▲ After the opening of the Xinghua Three Dams, the water depth on the plains reached one zhang, and all the fields in the territory were submerged, totaling 4 million mu. Each mu of good land was worth approximately 20 yuan, resulting in a total loss of approximately 80 million yuan. On August 26th, strong winds and heavy rain caused thousands of village weirs in the four rural areas to collapse. Whole villages were boarding boats. The Lao Weir, Zhong Weir, Shuifeng Weir, and Heta Weir in the northeastern townships, as well as the Laoren Weir and Sanjiao Weir connecting to Yancheng, were successively breached. Houses, livestock, and the newly harvested early rice were all swept away. There was not a single dry patch of land for over a hundred li in all directions. Even the highest point in the county seat was submerged to the waist. To this day, the dike breaches have not been closed, and the water level continues to rise by two or three cun each day. Winter is approaching, and tens of thousands of victims will succumb to hunger and cold.

News from the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association

The Yangzhou Branch is Officially Established

The association received a letter from President Dai Xiangmen of the Chinese branch and President So Hing-yan of the Western branch of the Yangzhou branch, reporting that the Yangzhou branch was established on September 5th. The address is the Zhongfu Gospel Church on Duozijie Street in Yangzhou. Because many public groups have come to Yangzhou for relief distribution, it is difficult to reach everyone. The branch plans to focus on remote disaster areas, while also paying attention to the severely affected areas of Gaoyou and Shaobo, adhering to the principle of being pragmatic.

▲ Hongkou Donation Collection Agency

Because there are many enthusiastic donors from all walks of life, but those far away still suffer from inconvenience, the association has already asked the Nanshi branch of the Bank of China to collect donations on its behalf. Yesterday, it also asked Mr. Chen Zisheng of the Hongkou Central Trust Company to collect donations for the association.

▲ Donations from Chinese Staff of Brunner Mond & Co.

Yesterday, the Chinese staff of the British merchant Brunner Mond & Co. collected and remitted 1,052 yuan to the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association for urgent relief distribution.

Anhui Relief Workers Carry Out Urgent Relief in Central Anhui

Anhui relief worker Xu Guozhi came to Shanghai and reported on the relief distribution in Wuhe and Fengtai, and also carried out urgent relief in central Anhui in a telegram that said:

To the committee members of the Shanghai Renji Hall Urgent Relief Association and Chairman Xu:

The representatives of the four counties have not arrived for a long time due to rotation issues and damaged telegraph poles. Guozhi is aware that the victims are eagerly awaiting relief. Fortunately, Pu Xiansan, the chairman of the Fengtai Chamber of Commerce, came from Shanghai to Bengbu and returned to the county to find a solution. Please ask relief friend Li Qinlian to go to the county together to investigate and distribute relief with local groups. Guozhi and relief friend Zhou Xuelin went to Wuhe via Linhuai during the winter. They immediately consulted with the county government and the flood relief committee on methods of investigation and distribution, leaving Mr. Zhou to handle the work in Wuhe. Guozhi returned to Bengbu and then went to Shouying and other counties with relief friend Li to negotiate. Then, he went to Anqing to carry out urgent relief in central Anhui. Xu Guozhi kowtows, Jiang.

Continued Reports of Floods in Various Counties of Anhui

The entire city of Datong is several chi deep in water. Countless people and animals are drifting away. The collapse of houses is heard every day. The citizens have no clothing or food, and their situation is dire.

▲ The dikes in Qianshan have all been breached, and countless houses have collapsed.

▲ The fields in Qiupu have all been swept away, and countless houses have collapsed. The water depth in the plains is more than one zhang.

▲ In Shexian, mountain floods have erupted, and the fields have been completely lost.

▲ In Huoshan, continuous rain has caused a disaster, drowning countless people and animals.

▲ The Haikouzhou dike line outside the west gate of Huaining is approximately forty li long, the land is approximately 30,000 to 40,000 mu, and there are 10,000 residents. On the night of July 24th, the northwest embankment breached, and the water surged like a mountain collapsing and the sea overturning. It was at night, and the residents, along with their grain, livestock, and equipment, were washed away. Hundreds of people drowned. The Guangren Weir, which was the first to collapse, had a northern embankment that was over seventy zhang long. There were still dozens of people on the embankments, trying to salvage them, but most of them drowned. Only a small firewood boat remained, and three people who were trying to salvage the situation survived on the embankment that had not been breached.

▲ The essence of the weir fields in Langxi has been submerged, affecting tens of thousands of victims. Death is rampant, and they are still trapped in the water.

▲ National Medical Association Forms Disaster Relief Medical Team

The National Medical Association held its eighteenth joint meeting of directors and supervisors the night before last, and Zhu Nanshan and Guo Boliang were elected as chairmen. After completing the formalities, the following matters were discussed:

(1) It was reported that the disaster victims arriving in Shanghai were suffering from pitiful illnesses, and the members requested the association to organize a medical team to provide medical care. How should this be handled? It was resolved that the association would organize two disaster relief medical teams, A and B, to provide free treatment to disaster victims in the North and South Shanghai areas. Zhu Nanshan, Hu Fo, Xu Shoupeng, Guo Boliang, Xia Chongguang, Weng Tiansheng, Chen Shu'an, Ren Nongxuan, Zhang Hongyuan and other nine people were appointed as members of Team A, and doctors Ding Zhongying, Zhang Zanchen, Yang Yanhe, Wu Keqian, Fu Yongyan, Yan Cangshan, Shen Shirong, Huang Qizhou, Bao Tianbai, etc., were appointed as members of Team B. The doctors will carry medicines and powders with them every day to treat the disaster victims in the North and South Shanghai reception centers. If there are seriously ill patients, they will be sent to the hospital for treatment with the consent of the patients. The herbal medicine will also be decocted and distributed by the association in consultation with the Chinese pharmacies to facilitate treatment. In addition to preparing a letter to report to the municipal disaster relief reception center office, the health department, etc., a meeting of the medical team will be held at the association's office tonight. It is also heard that the office has replied by letter, and the association has been granted permission to open a Chinese medicine department in the reception center, which will be managed by the association.

▲ French Concession Taxpayers Association Solicits Clothing and Bedding

▲ A Large Number of Fresh Steamed Buns Distributed to the Disaster Victims

Mr. Xia Guoliang, director of the Laoximen West District Fire Brigade, saved more than 100 yuan from the district members' dinner expenses, purchased a large amount of flour, and hired more than 20 cooks to work day and night at the Ximen Guandi Temple. The Jiangyuan Warship Has Sunk

Technicians Can Arrive Today

Still Possible to Salvage and Escape Danger

▲ Huge Hole

The Jiangyuan warship of the First Fleet of the Navy ran aground on a reef while chasing pirates in Xinghua Bay, Fuzhou. It has been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the Jiangyuan warship ran aground in the head cabin bottom, and there was a large hole of six or seven chi square in the reef. Sea water rushed into the cabin, first flooding the head cabin, and then affecting the second cabin. Although the soldiers in the ship tried their best to pump water, it was ineffective due to the excessive damage. Within three hours, the entire ship was submerged in sea water.

▲ Jiangyuan Warship Sinks in the Sea

Around 6 p.m., the engine room of the Jiangyuan warship was also flooded, the boiler went out, all the lights in the ship went out, and the machine stopped, unable to start. The rescue warship sent by Commander Chen Jiliang had arrived. The Jiangyuan warship captain took out some of the important documents, and at 6:30 p.m., the ship sank into the sea.

▲ Salvage in Progress

The salvage technicians and divers of the Mitsui Company, who were requested by the Naval Headquarters in Shanghai, can arrive in Fuzhou today. After inspecting Xinghua Bay, they will discuss salvage. According to reliable information, although the Jiangyuan sank, it was fortunately stranded on the reef and has not sunk to the bottom of the sea. It is still possible to salvage it. However, the hole is very large, and the repair and salvage costs will require more than 300,000 yuan.

▲ Ship Damage

The Jiangyuan warship was built at the Nagasaki Mitsubishi Shipyard. The entire ship is made of steel plates, with a displacement of 700 tons. The cost, including the interior layout, was 1 million yuan. The ship has only been built for 15 years. At the current gold price, 1 million is not enough. The personal belongings of the officers and soldiers in the ship have not been retrieved, and the losses are also significant.

Overseas Chinese Expelled from Mexico Return to China

Arriving in Shanghai on the 28th

A wave of anti-Chinese sentiment has occurred in Mexico, and our overseas Chinese have suffered heavy losses. They have now withdrawn from Mexico and are returning to their homeland by ship. The first batch of overseas Chinese departing from Mexico for Shanghai totaled 184 people, mostly from Fujian and Guangdong. They have taken a ship to New York and transferred to the Dalai Shipping Company's President Monroe ship to return to Shanghai. According to a telegram received yesterday, the batch of overseas Chinese has arrived in San Francisco and is expected to arrive in Shanghai at 9 a.m. on the 28th of this month. It is heard that some of them will land in Shanghai, and some will disembark in Hong Kong.

Chinese Not Allowed to Go to Japan

Obstructed and Expelled

▲ Chinese Passengers to Japan Obstructed: Since Japan recognized Shanghai as a port with epidemic diseases, the restrictions on Chinese people going to Japan are extremely strict, and the inspection is very severe. Third-class passengers are not allowed to go to Yokohama, and large mail ships do not carry Chinese people. This time, the Japanese postal company's ship Kasado Maru went to Japan, and among the Shanghai Chinese passengers on board, there were thirty-five Chinese sailors hired by British ships and more than ten Chinese travelers. Unexpectedly, when the ship arrived at Moji, one of the sailors named Ren Haixiang vomited in the ship due to seasickness. The Japanese ship doctor considered it to be real cholera and did not allow all Chinese passengers on the ship to go ashore. They were detained on the sea surface outside Moji Port for seven days and nights and subjected to various unbearable examinations. Other Chinese people who did not vomit were also implicated and have not been released yet.

▲ Chinese People Expelled from Returning to Japan: Chinese people Chen Zhikui, Sun Yushan, Pan Caixing, Mei Louren, Wu Xiangyao, and Doctor Yang, etc., were engaged in the kimono business in Japan. This time, they went to Japan from Shanghai. When they arrived at a port in Japan, the Japanese maritime police did not allow any Chinese people to go ashore and expelled them back to their home country. The travel expenses and ship tickets of each person were deducted by the shipping company according to the amount of the prepaid deposit, so the expelled people suffered a great loss.

Regular Flights on the Beijing-Ping Line Resumed

Flights Between the Two Places on the Morning of the 17th of This Month

The resumption date of the China Aviation Corporation's Beijing-Ping line was originally scheduled for the 22nd of last month, but it was postponed again because most of the route was obstructed by water. A few days ago, the company sent Nie Kaiyi, the director of the flight crew, by plane to the north to inspect the current situation of the stations along the route. Yesterday (the 11th) morning, Mr. Nie telegraphed the company from Ping, reporting that there was no standing water at the stations along the route, and all the necessary equipment at each station was ready, so regular flights could be resumed immediately. After receiving the telegram, the company, led by Secretary He Zhijing, discussed the resumption date of the Beijing-Ping line and decided to start flights between Beijing and Ping on the morning of the 17th of this month. The aircraft currently flying, there are four Stinson-type aircraft at the Longhua Main Station in Shanghai, all of which have been repaired. On the 14th and 15th of this month, they will fly to Beijing Station to prepare for the resumption of flights. The resumption of flights will still be dedicated to carrying mail, and the date for carrying passengers has not yet been determined. Each flight will have two pilots, one to fly the plane and one as an assistant, all of whom are Chinese.

Jiangsu Counties Telegraphically Urge to Stop Opening the East Dam

The East Dam, seventy miles west of Liyang County, is the lifeline of the Taihu Lake basin. Once opened, the provinces south of the Yangtze River will be submerged. Recently, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, in order to drain the accumulated water from Gaoyou and Shaobo in northern Jiangsu, decided to open the East Dam. When the news came, the counties along Taihu Lake in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces successively petitioned to stop it. The Shanghai Suzhou Fellow Villagers Association, the Pingjiang Guild Hall, the Dongting Xishan and Jinting Association Board of Directors, the Wuxi Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association, and the Dongting Dongshan Association Board of Directors in this city have all convened emergency meetings yesterday. After in-depth discussions, they all vowed to fight to the death to ensure the integrity of the dam and prevent it from being opened or collapsing.

Hesheng Wheel Damaged and Returned to Shanghai

Fearing Dangerous Accidents En Route

Matters of Life and Property are of Utmost Importance

After the Guang Sheng Wheel accident, Jardine Matheson & Co. purchased two Dutch wheels, named Xin Hesheng and Xin Mingsheng, each with 3,000 tons, to be dispatched to Shanghai to run the South China class to temporarily replace the Guang Sheng into ascending classes. This time, the Hesheng Wheel was loaded with a large number of goods from Shanghai, such as wheat flour, piece goods, cotton yarn, cigarettes, etc., and was heading to Hong Kong and Guangdong. There were also more than one hundred passengers on board. Unexpectedly, when the ship was halfway, the parts in its engine suddenly broke down. Upon inspection by the ship owner, it was determined that it could not sail. Deeply concerned that an extremely dangerous accident might occur en route, which would have a significant impact on the lives and property of the entire ship, they telegraphed Shanghai yesterday, reporting the return to Shanghai to repair the engine parts, and then set sail again to ensure safety. The ship is expected to arrive this morning. The goods will not be unloaded. The company has decided to send workers on board to complete the repairs and then set sail immediately.

Peng Liren Reports on Disaster Situation

Peng Liren, the Standing Committee Member of the County Executive Committee, reported to the Provincial Rectification Committee, stating, "Regarding the instructions from your committee No. 21076, to conduct a detailed investigation of the disaster situation and report it truthfully, etc., most of the farmland in this county is planted with cotton, and the rest is planted with rice. In mid-July of this year, continuous rainfall for more than ten days, just when the cotton was bearing fruit and the rice seedlings were growing, caused the cotton bolls to rot and the rice seedlings to be submerged due to excessive heat. Although not all of it was abandoned, according to the results of the investigation, the harvest is expected to be 60% less than in a bumper year. Extending to late August, a typhoon passed through Shanghai, and agricultural crops along the coast suffered another major blow. Based on the experience of farmers, the harvest this year, if there are no more disasters, may be only 10% to 20% of a good harvest. The losses, if estimated in silver dollars, would be about 200,000 yuan. The county is now actively seeking relief methods. In accordance with the previous order, this document is prepared for your review."

Mulberry Trees Submerged in Jiangsu, Zhejiang and Other Provinces

The Ministry Orders Advance Planning

The Ministry of Industry is investigating the damage to mulberry trees caused by water in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other provinces to seek remedies. The order is as follows: "For the purpose of issuing orders, it is hereby notified that this year's rainfall has caused disasters. Most of the low-lying mulberry fields have been submerged, resulting in a poor mulberry leaf harvest. Autumn silkworms this year will suffer from a lack of feed. Those who plant silkworms cannot raise them, causing deep concern. However, the disaster that has already occurred is difficult to remedy, and the future harm should be prevented in advance. If mulberry trees are permanently submerged, it is difficult to guarantee that they will not wither due to waterlogging. A detailed investigation should be conducted in areas where mulberry trees have been damaged, and plans should be made early. More mulberry seedlings should be cultivated to prepare for replanting and maintain the silk industry. This order is hereby issued to the bureau to comply with and implement, and to submit the implementation details to the ministry for review as needed."

Working Hours Issue in the Printing Industry

Labor Concedes, Extends to Eight and a Half Hours

The printing industry union previously proposed amending the labor-management contract, which dragged on for two months. A work stoppage once occurred in the middle. The conditions have now been mediated by the Shanghai Social Bureau. As a result, regarding the issue of working hours, the labor side insisted on the original agreement of eight hours, while the management side still wanted to restore nine hours. The two sides argued fiercely, regarding it as the most important focus of all the conditions, so no agreement was signed. The union held a city-wide representative meeting yesterday to discuss working hours. All the representatives firmly upheld the original agreement of eight hours. After strenuous persuasion, it was decided to concede and extend the working hours to eight and a half hours, not to exceed that. It is unknown whether the management side will accept this.

China Merchants Bureau Pier 5 Employees Present Seven Demands

The China Merchants Bureau's unresolved case with the Pier 5 Employees Union is accumulating more and more. The Employees Union, repeatedly blamed by its members, has had no choice but to convene meetings to discuss and decide to present seven minimum demands to the head office, and to organize a Seven Demands Committee to take charge. The Seven Demands Committee has also met in recent days and officially sent the seven demands back to the head office yesterday. Yu Xianting, Xue Yinda, Zhang Guiqing, Wu Jucai, and Xia Yinxu were appointed to form a presidium, with Yu Xianting as the head of security, Zhang Guiqing as the head of the propaganda section, Ye Yufu and Wang Jielu as deputy heads, Xue Yinkui as the head of the investigation section, and Hu Maolin and Zhou Xinbao as deputy heads. The situation is serious and the work is intense, with a strong momentum to not rest until the goal is achieved. The seven demands are attached: (1) All employees of Pier 5 should be given bonuses equally based on the principle of equality. (2) All employees of Pier 5 should be provided with meals by the bureau, in accordance with the same treatment as employees of the head office. (3) Wu Bingru, Zhou Hesheng, Jin Peisun, Feng Abiao, Jiang Ronggui, and the other five employees who were transferred from the pier should all be restored to their original positions, and it should be guaranteed that similar incidents will not occur in the future. (4) Zhou Xinbao, Shi Qisheng, Geng Asan, and the other three employees who were fired should all be restored to their original positions, and it should be guaranteed that similar incidents will not occur in the future. (5) New personnel who are unfamiliar with the pier situation should all leave the pier. (6) According to Article 10 of the treatment conditions stipulated on November 21, 1928, all employees of Pier 5 who have not yet joined the union should be ordered by the bureau to join the union immediately. If they still refuse to join, the bureau should immediately revoke their positions to respect the treaty. (7) Employees who bring family members to live in dormitories should be immediately revoked their positions by the bureau.

National Seaport Quarantine Office Report on Cholera Prevention

No. 7

The National Seaport Quarantine Office issued the seventh cholera prevention report: (1) During the week from August 30 to September 5, the cholera symptoms discovered in this city increased compared to before, but they were all mild and easily treated. According to the investigation report, 48 people were found in the Chinese area, all of whom have been cured. Eleven people were found in the Public Concession, one of whom has died. Eight people were found in the French Concession, all of whom have been cured. In total, there were 67 patients last week, and only one person died. (2) According to the investigation, about 25,000 people from Hankou have come to Shanghai to seek refuge, and one-third of them have no place to live and are temporarily living in temporary shelters. Recent reports in various newspapers have made many rumors about the shelters, but they are not true. The authorities have already taken preventive measures, so no cholera or other infectious diseases have been found in the shelters. Although cases of dysentery have been found, they are not new cases. Dysentery is a common disease in the Yangtze River basin and is not surprising. Director of the Health Bureau Hu Hongji and his police assistants are responsible for the medical affairs of the shelters. (3) The quarantine medical officers in Hankou, Nanjing, and Wusong have implemented inspections. The shipping companies for the civilian ships entering and leaving Shanghai and Hankou in each port are also assisting enthusiastically, which can reduce the import of infectious diseases to a minimum. (4) The first meeting of the Water Disaster Relief Committee was attended by 150 Chinese and foreign leaders, who announced that they had donated 2.5 million yuan for relief. One-seventh of the 7 million yuan relief fund is planned to be used for health work, which is very important. (5) Liu Ruiheng, director of the Health and Epidemic Prevention Group of the Relief Committee, has convened leaders from the Chinese and foreign medical communities to jointly discuss the direction of epidemic prevention work, in order to achieve practical results economically. (6) From April 1 to August 31 of this year, according to the latest statistics, the number of people who have received cholera vaccinations is as follows: Shanghai City 474,890 people, Public Concession 133,761 people, and French Concession 47,719 people. According to a detailed investigation report, none of those who have received vaccinations have contracted cholera or other infectious diseases.

Page 15

Local News Two

Baoshan Seawall in Danger

The Baoshan seawall has not been repaired for three to five years. This year, after the hurricane high tide on August 25th of the lunar calendar, many dangerous situations have occurred. The engineering progress of the seawall office is slow, and the people of Baoshan are urgently appealing. According to the seawall inspection report on September 9th by Yuan Chushu, a member of the county's seawall protection committee: "On the morning of September 9th, we invited Committee Member Tao Qingfeng, Committee Member Jin Qiyuan, Representative Mr. Li Junbi, and Mr. Xiluo to depart from outside the north gate of Baoshan and inspect the seawall along the line. At 2 p.m., we arrived at the junction of Beichuan Sha and Taicang, about thirty miles away. Except for a section of four or five miles from Beishitang to Xiaosha Bei, which has a rising beach, and a section of about seven or eight miles from north of Huangyao to Xiaochuan Sha, which has a rising beach and is safe, the rest, from Chenhuabin to the north of Wuyuedun and the southern section of Huangyao, is about twenty miles long. Only a few sections newly built between 1919 and 1925 are still intact. In addition, dangers can occur everywhere. The construction of this seawall is divided into three parts. The outermost part is a breakwater built with cypress stone. The inner part is a stone embankment built with cypress stone, several feet wide, forming a slope. The innermost part is a regular embankment with cypress wood and stone on the outside and earth and mud filled on the inside, about three or four feet wide. Most of the cypress wood and stones in this twenty-mile long regular embankment have been washed away, leaving no trace, and half of the embankment's soil has also been washed away. The most dangerous sections are the three sections of the Gulongdun embankment, where there are now more than ten cracks across the embankment. These cracks are formed under the embankment, and only a small hole can be seen on the embankment surface. Looking down, the situation below can be seen, but it is not easily visible on the surface, which is the most dangerous. If these cracks are filled with water from the high tide, they can collapse immediately. North of the Lion Forest Fort, from Zhangjiazhai to Xuejiatan, there are more than ten places where only a foot or less of the soil embankment remains. The same is true for Niutoujing. As for the embankment around Beishidong, the water flow is rapid due to the tide entering and exiting the stone cave, and the construction of the embankment was previously stronger. However, a section of the embankment north of the cave, several tens of feet long, has been washed away and is in a dangerous situation. There is a section of about one hundred and several tens of feet at Wuyuedun, and its washed-away situation is similar to that of Xuejiatan. Seeing this situation, it is necessary to use tens of thousands of cypress trees, two to three hundred thousand burlap bags, and four to five thousand workers for emergency repairs in order to complete the dangerous work before the eighteenth day of the eighth lunar month. If an accident occurs during the high tide period on the third day of the eighth lunar month, not only will all previous efforts be in vain, but it will also be impossible to protect. We asked the villagers along the seawall why the seawall was in such a dangerous state. They all replied that it had not been repaired once in the past four or five years since 1927. Therefore, there were already signs of danger last autumn. When we inspected the seawall, we saw about one hundred workers in Zhangjiazhai and Xuejiatan driving cypress trees and filling soil with burlap bags. However, at Wuyuedun, there were only twenty or thirty workers scattered around unloading and filling soil. The progress of the project was very slow. Moreover, we saw that there were not many cypress trees and burlap bags at Xuejiatan and Zhangjiazhai. When we returned to Bao in the evening, we saw few cypress trees and burlap bags piled up in front of the seawall office, which was not enough to use for emergency repairs. Moreover, the cypress trees were shorter and thinner than those used in the past. Therefore, the cypress trees driven in at Xuejiatan and Zhangzhai were about three or four feet lower than the old cypress trees that remained. I am afraid that piling up sandbags in this way will not be enough to resist the high tide. In addition, we did not see any workers working at the other dangerous places. When we returned at 5 p.m., we met Section Chief Xue at Lion Forest and asked about the number of workers currently working on emergency repairs. He said there were 200 people. We asked why the cypress trees were short and thin. He said that the price of wood was expensive, so he had no choice but to use this. We asked why the dangerous work that occurred last year was not repaired last year, leading to this year's great danger. He said that he had requested funding last year, but the requests were repeatedly denied. It was not as good as this year's Chairman Ye and Construction Director Sun, who were able to grant the requests. Xiluo and others saw this situation and felt extremely worried. According to the lunar calendar, there are two high tide periods in August, one lasting only four or five days and the other lasting only eighteen or nineteen days. If there is another hurricane with a high tide like the one on August 25th of the lunar calendar, how can we be spared? We must order the responsible persons to rush the work and speed up the repairs, and seek assistance from all parties to proceed. Therefore, we submit this report and request that an emergency meeting be convened quickly to discuss countermeasures for remedial action. This report is hereby made. Yuan Xiluo, Tao Qingfeng, Jin Qiyuan."

Young Man Commits Suicide in Wusongkou, Huangpu River

A Suicide Note Was Found Beside Him

At about 11:30 a.m. yesterday, a male corpse wearing a suit was found floating in the Huangpu River in front of the South Stone Fort at Wusongkou. The fortress headquarters notified the Wusong Lifesaving Bureau, which dispatched a lifesaving patrol boat to retrieve the corpse and take it to the beach. Gu Danchao, the director of the bureau, sent someone to investigate and found that the corpse was about 20 years old, with a round face, and his hair parted in two. He was wearing a purple flannel suit, gray flannel pants, a white linen shirt, blue sneakers, and black socks. There were no wounds on his body, and his face was not yet decomposed. A suicide note was found beside him, indicating that he had committed suicide by drowning. However, the name and address of the recipient written on the envelope were not very clear, so it was impossible to notify them. The charitable hall will temporarily collect and bury the body, marking the number for relatives to claim. There was also a note, a foreign thread coin purse containing two small foreign coins, eight copper coins, a rubber eraser, and a green pencil. The suicide note is transcribed as follows:

The envelope is addressed to Mr. Liu ○ Liang, ○○ School, Fanhwangdu, Shanghai. Sent by Liu Ji, September 9. The letter reads: "Dear brother, it is unbearable to say goodbye forever. This morning, I received Mr. Yu's lecture, and my heart felt like it was pierced. After thinking again and again, if seeking knowledge is like this for young people, then what will the old do? I am truly a fool, and I have no face to see people. The harm to my foolish brother is especially painful. Dear brother, it is unbearable to say goodbye forever. I hope you will study hard and take care of yourself. The pillar of our family in the future depends on you. This is my deepest hope. I also hope that when my expenses are brought here, you will give 10.2 yuan to you, 20 yuan to Chen Lunxue, and 60 yuan to Bao Yi and Bao Shu, half each, and send the rest back to my father's house. Otherwise, you and the others can use it together, which is also fine. Dear brother, farewell forever. Please take care. Ya ○ said." Another note reads: "Dear brother Zishan, I sent a letter yesterday. I don't know if you have received it."

The Strong-Arm Tactics of Four Detectives

Dragging Pedestrians into Alleys

Extorting Money in Every Way Possible

The Police Department Prosecutes on Three Charges

Three Detectives Admit to Wrongdoing

Jiang Youming, residing in a bungalow on Connaught Road, was riding his bicycle home at 6:15 PM on the 1st of this month when he passed near the Baolong Hospital on Baker Road. He happened to encounter Guo Baolin, badge number 3217, Zhu Yigui, badge number 1637, Zhan Yande, badge number 2869, and Gong Ruilin, badge number 3086, all Chinese detectives from the Xinzha Police Station, who were searching pedestrians. Jiang was stopped and searched by Detective Guo. A lottery ticket was found in Jiang’s pocket. Detective Guo immediately dragged him into a nearby alley and demanded money for his release. They took the three silver dollars and two paper dollars that Jiang had in his pocket. Not satisfied, they forced Jiang to take off his pants and pawn them at the nearby Ruikang Pawnshop for two silver dollars, which Guo took before releasing Jiang. At 8:20 PM, Jiang reported the incident to the Xinzha Police Station. Chinese Detective Sergeants Bao Yongshun and Zhang Wenjun arrested the four detectives and had Jiang identify them among a group of other detectives. Jiang immediately pointed out Detective Guo. The sergeants detained Guo, Zhu, Zhan, and Gong. Three silver dollars were found on Guo, and Jiang identified one of them as his own, recognizing a black mark on the coin's surface. Due to the late hour, the police station could not investigate thoroughly that night, so they applied to the court for temporary detention the next day. Yesterday morning, the police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, filed a public prosecution with the First Special District Court, charging the four detectives with robbery under Article 348 of the Criminal Law, abuse of official duty under Article 140, and dereliction of duty under Article 129, requesting severe punishment. At 9 AM, Magistrate Wu Tingqi opened the court to question the suspects. Jiang Youming testified about the events, stating that the paper found by Detective Guo was a note from his uncle asking him to pick up a raincoat on Sima Road, not a lottery ticket. Sergeants Bao and Zhang testified about the investigation and Jiang's identification of Detective Guo at the police station. At this point, Police Lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that Guo, Zhu, and Zhan had all written confessions at the police station, while Gong denied the charges. The confessions were presented to the court. When questioned, Detective Guo admitted to the incident and claimed that they had also discovered someone carrying opium. After negotiating with Inspector Connor, Western detective number 321, for 50 dollars, the Western detective ordered their release. The four of them then split the money, receiving seven and a half dollars each. When questioned, Zhu Yigui, Zhan Yande, and Gong Ruilin all admitted to releasing the opium carrier but denied involvement in the Jiang Youming case. They stated that they were under the control of the Western detective, and they had to release the suspect if he ordered them to do so. Magistrate Wu Tingqi reviewed the testimonies and ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody for further questioning.

### Conviction for Fundraising Scam

Guo Biao Reports on the Deceptive Donation Process

Zheng Youqing Sentenced to Five Months Imprisonment

Zheng Youqing (also known as Bo Xun), the son of Zheng A Yuan, the owner of the Juchang Pawnshop at 112 Wusong Road, neglected his duties, left his family, and wandered aimlessly for several years. Last month, he suddenly arrived in Shanghai from Hankou with a young woman named Tang Jinghua and others, staying in Room 123 of the Dadong Hotel. Using the false name of the "Guangdong Overseas Chinese Hankou Disaster Relief Group," he, along with Lin Shanbo and a woman named Zheng Wangshi, went out to solicit donations. They also placed advertisements to recruit contact staff. Someone discovered their fraudulent scheme and reported it to the Lao Zha Police Station. Detective Wang Yingjie arrested Zheng and the other three individuals, confiscating counterfeit donation books, receipts, seals, and collected donations. They were taken to the First Special District Court, which ordered them each to post a 1,000-dollar bail and conducted an investigation. The previous report detailed the situation. It is now known that only Zheng Wangshi was bailed out that day, while the others remained in custody. Detective Wang continued his investigation and discovered that Zheng Wangshi owned the Runchang Clothing Store at 122 Wusong Road, and her husband was a relative of Zheng Youqing. Lin Shanbo, whose original name was Huang Binghua, was a surveyor of damaged goods on the Blue Funnel Line at the Taikoo Wharf. Both were recruited by Zheng Youqing after arriving in Shanghai to join the fundraising group. The 41 dollars in donations they had collected were also investigated. The detective visited the names listed in the donation book, such as dentist Wang Bingji at 50 Beijing Road, dentist Li Xinquan at 685 North Sichuan Road, and Zheng Huili, all of whom confirmed they had been defrauded. During the previous court hearing, Zheng Youqing claimed that he had raised 6,000 dollars from the Guang Zhao Public Association and that the association had sent Cheng Bingkui with him to Hankou to distribute the relief funds. However, Zheng had stayed in Shanghai due to other business, and Cheng had gone alone. After this was reported in the newspapers, the association stated that it was far from the truth. Therefore, when Magistrate Cheng Shangfeng continued the trial yesterday morning, Guo Biao, a director of the association, testified in court. Guo stated that on the 27th of last month, Zheng Youqing suddenly reported to the association, claiming to be a representative of the Hankou Guangdong Overseas Chinese Hankou Disaster Relief Group, and requested donations. At that time, the entire board was discussing the Wuhan flood relief efforts. They allowed him to participate, as he had just come from the disaster area and was familiar with the situation. He then presented a letter stating the disaster situation in detail and requested the association to publish an advertisement recognizing his fundraising group as the official relief organization for Guangdong overseas Chinese in Hankou. The directors, suspecting his motives, refused his request. The meeting resulted in a donation of 6,000 dollars, and Cheng Bingkui was sent to Hankou to distribute the funds, which were to be collected at the Wing On Company branch in Hankou. Zheng Youqing was not sent with him. After seeing the report in the newspapers, the association sent a letter to Cheng to investigate. They received a telegram in response stating that there was no such organization in Hankou. The address they provided was also investigated, and there were no residents with the names of the defendants. The only official Guangdong organization in Hankou was the Overseas Chinese Commerce Association, which was responsible for all relief efforts. Representatives from those who had been defrauded, such as Wang Bingji, also appeared in court to testify about the fraudulent donation scheme and the amount of their losses. When questioned, Zheng Youqing claimed that he had witnessed the severe flood and organized a fundraising group with ten comrades. He and Tang Jinghua, Lin Xiao Bai, and Chen Sanhong were sent to Shanghai to raise funds. He and Tang remained in Shanghai to solicit donations, while Lin and Chen went to Southeast Asia. Lin Xiao Bai and Zheng Wangshi both testified that Zheng had recruited them to help. Tang's testimony matched Zheng's. Police Lawyer Qian Xunji stated that Tang and Zheng appeared to be in a marital relationship but were not married. After arguments from defendant lawyers Huang Yupi and Huang Xiubo, Magistrate Cheng declared that the defendants were guilty of joint fraud. Zheng was sentenced to five months imprisonment, Tang to three months imprisonment, and Lin and Zheng Wangshi were each fined 400 dollars. The donation books were confiscated.
