Fundraising Under False Pretenses

Bearing the Seal of the West Shanghai Charity Group

Investigation by the Urgent Relief Association's Propaganda Team

The Shanghai Urgent Relief Association's Propaganda Team for the provinces affected by flooding noticed someone distributing donation letters with the seal of the West Shanghai Charity Group in the Xinzha Road area, soliciting donations door-to-door in an attempt to collect money. They immediately sent representatives to the West Shanghai Charity Group in Tangjiawan to investigate. The group's communications director received them and, when asked whether the group had sent anyone out to solicit donations, stated that they were unaware. When shown the original donation letter and its seal, which appeared similar to the group's seal, they agreed to inquire and respond the following day. The investigators asked for the minutes of any fundraising discussions and requested to see the seal for verification. They were told that the group had not held any meetings to discuss sending letters for donations. The seal was in the custody of the documents clerk and could not be obtained for comparison. The matter might be the action of an individual member, which was unknown. When asked about the group's leaders, they were told that the director was Liang Yegong. Accompanied by Wang, they went to inquire with Xu in detail. Xu stated that the group had absolutely not taken such action and that someone must be using their name under false pretenses. He agreed to investigate the matter within the group.

Paul Discusses the Utility of Automobiles

Remarks at a Rotary Club Luncheon

The Shanghai Rotary Club held a luncheon at the Navy YMCA on Sichuan Road the day before yesterday and invited Paul, from the American Automobile Trade Association, to speak on the importance of automobile transportation. He stated that not long ago, the United States had only four automobiles, one of which was used as a promotional tool in a circus. Today, there are 26 million automobiles, more than telephones. It would be easy for everyone in the country to travel by automobile, with one car for every five people. They could set off at the same time and travel to remote towns. Long-distance buses now run regularly between cities as far apart as New York and San Francisco, and they are as fast as trains. Automobile garages in large cities are located in 22-story buildings, with elevators for raising and lowering cars. Specially built automobile tunnels cross rivers and streams to supplement bridges. Even in crowded cities like New York, elevated highways are being planned for fast automobile traffic. The reason automobiles have developed so much in America is that people have adopted a new concept, recognizing the importance of time. They understand that a large part of our lives is spent on travel (i.e., the "travel" in the necessities of life: clothing, food, housing, and travel). By saving time on travel, more time can be devoted to other endeavors. People want to do things with the least cost and the greatest efficiency. "Cost" refers not only to money but also to labor and time. Therefore, in terms of transportation, rickshaws are the most expensive because, although the fare is cheap, the cost of the journey is high when the distance traveled and the time spent are combined. The German automobile manufacturing industry a few years ago provides an example. At that time, German wages were low, only one-sixth of American wages, but American-made automobiles could compete with German automobiles in the market because the United States used machines to manufacture automobiles ten times faster, reducing costs. To utilize automobiles for transportation, good roads are essential. Road construction is the primary task in developing automobile transportation. Fortunately, automobiles are productive, and with good policies, the cost of road construction can be easily offset. For example, after automobiles are introduced, poor people can travel to more distant locations to purchase cheaper goods. The increased tax burden from road construction can be offset in this way. Road construction can be financed by issuing bonds, with tax revenue used as collateral for repaying the principal and interest. Today, China is gradually adopting the concept of time, and road construction is underway. Passengers and goods are increasingly transported by automobiles. As transportation becomes more convenient, the waste of time will gradually decrease.

Urging Payment of Overdue 1927 Land Tax

During the 1927 year when the city and county were not yet separated, there were still significant overdue land taxes. Although the County Finance Bureau has repeatedly issued strict orders to collect these taxes, they have not yet been fully recovered. It has been found that most of these overdue taxes were misappropriated by local security chiefs and others. The County Finance Bureau's authority does not extend to those who misappropriated the funds, as they are now under the jurisdiction of the city. Director Wang of the Bureau has instructed the original officials responsible for collecting the taxes to press for payment, and ordered a separate investigation of those who misappropriated the funds, to be reported for prosecution to ensure national revenue.

Public Bus Collides with Tram

Tram number 188, running between Jing'an Temple and Bazichang, was traveling east on Nanjing Road at 3:05 PM yesterday when it approached the western end of the baseball field. A public bus, number 15086, was traveling in the same direction when the driver carelessly collided with the entrance gate of the tram. The loud crash startled the passengers. Fortunately, the brakes were applied quickly, preventing a major disaster and no one was injured. However, the tram's iron gate and the front of the bus were slightly damaged.

Silk Factory Debt Case Results in Lawsuit

Wu Songyan and Wei Zitang Held Responsible

Owed Debt of 110,000 Taels Must Be Repaid

Wu Songyan and Wei Zitang, silk factory shareholders from Wuxing, formerly representing various silk factories, borrowed 260,000 taels of silver, including interest, a total of 275,000 taels from Amidani, an Italian at the Bao Ke Foreign Firm. The loan was distributed as follows: 40,000 taels to the Dalun Silk Factory, 20,000 taels to the Yongfeng Silk Factory, and the remainder to the Jiulun Silk Factory. Later, Jiulun repaid 90,000 taels, but the remaining amount was not repaid. Amidani subsequently died. Recently, Amidani's representative, Fumagali, hired lawyer Yan Huilian and filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court against the Jiulun Silk Factory, identifying Wu and Wei as the owners of Jiulun, demanding repayment of 110,000 taels and associated legal costs. Wu and Wei hired lawyer Zhu Sifu to defend themselves, denying that they were the owners of the Jiulun Silk Factory. They claimed that Jiulun was a partnership with eight shareholders, including Chen Shuying, Chen Jingxian, Huang Xinsheng, Xu Shaobo, Zhu Jiling, and Cao Zipei in addition to Wu and Wei. They also claimed that the debt was owed by Jiulun, and all shareholders should be responsible for their share, not just Wu and Wei. Therefore, they requested that Chen Shuying and the others also be included as defendants. The Special Court had already held one hearing in the case, which was then adjourned. Yesterday morning, presiding judge Li Mo announced the verdict in the Ninth Civil Court, ruling against Wu and the others and ordering them to repay the outstanding 110,000 taels.

Yongfa Sandboat Robbed by Pirates

Six Abducted... Crew Injured... Cargo Robbed

The Gong Yongfa sandboat, owned by the Yongli Company, recently loaded timber in Fuzhou, worth over 60,000 taels of silver, for delivery to Yangzhou. Because the Shanghai office still had goods to be transported to the company's boat in Yangzhou, it arrived in Wusong on the 3rd of this month and anchored. Due to the large amount of cargo, it could not be loaded at once, so it set sail to Yangzhou to unload before returning to Shanghai to load more. On the afternoon of the 6th, while sailing off the coast of Haimen, it was suddenly attacked by a large group of pirates in three ships, sailing quickly with the wind. The pirates surrounded the sandboat. The crew of the sandboat, realizing the danger, ordered the sails to be raised and tried to escape. The pirates saw this and fired over ten shots at the sandboat, damaging the hull and injuring three crew members. The crew tried their best to escape the pirates but were pursued. Eventually, the smaller, faster pirate ships caught up with the sandboat, and the pirates, armed with guns and swords, swarmed aboard. Two pirates slipped and fell into the sea as they boarded the ship, enraging the others. They attacked the crew indiscriminately, injuring many more. They searched the captain's cabin, looting all the silver, ledgers, and a suitcase. They searched the crew and left no one unrobbed. One helmsman resisted and was shot and killed. Before leaving, they kidnapped the captain, Peng Guangyi, and two crew members, placing them on three separate pirate ships. They told the remaining crew to prepare 6,000 dollars for their ransom before sailing northeast. After the pirates left, the sandboat sailed to Liuhe, purchased a coffin for the slain helmsman, and sent the injured to the hospital. Yesterday, the Yongli Company received the report and sent representatives to Liuhe to investigate the robbery and report it to the water police for investigation and arrest.

Yang Linxiang Case Still Under Investigation

Yang Linxiang, a resident of Ayi Bridge, Meilong, Caohejing, was found dead, and the local court sent investigators. The deceased's wife, Yang Anan, claimed that her husband was scolded by Bai Yunzhang, her adoptive father, leading to his suicide by hanging. However, locals and officers from the Third Precinct of the Sixth District claimed that Yang Anan was promiscuous and the deceased did not have a steady job. The two did not get along, so she killed him by placing a bamboo dustpan over his neck and strangling him, rather than him committing suicide. Therefore, the court ordered the arrest and detention of Yang Anan. However, Xia Fuzhi, the deceased's brother, and Xie, the deceased's mother, have not filed a case or requested a re-examination of the body. The court has summoned those involved for questioning to determine the facts of the case.

Identity of Unidentified Male Corpse

Name Card Reads "Cheng Xianggui, Hao Xiangqiu"

Yesterday, an unidentified male corpse was discovered floating on the water near Lujiazui Wharf. The deceased appeared to be around 30 years old, wearing a striped linen suit, a white shirt, a white undershirt, a red and black floral tie, a leather belt, white socks, and black leather shoes. He had a flat-top haircut. The corpse was floating up and down with the current. A patrol boat from the Tongren Fuyuan Hall Rescue Bureau in the Nanshi district spotted the body, retrieved it, and brought it to the bureau in front of the South Wharf. Multiple name cards were found near the body, bearing the name "Cheng Xianggui, Hao Xiangqiu." However, the address and origin were not indicated. The bureau took photographs, prepared a coffin, and awaited the arrival of family members to identify the body.

Penalties for Failure to Affix Stamp Tax

Inspectors from the Stamp Tax Law Promotion Office of the National Government's Ministry of Finance discovered that four businesses, the Jin Feng Electric Store at 239 Mintini Road, the Zhen Changxiang Hardware Store at 80 Xingsheng Street, the Hengxing Store at 197 Avenue Dubail, and the Da Shanghai Socks Factory at 4 Jin Yili, Wangzhi Road, had failed to affix stamp tax stamps to their account books, violating the Stamp Tax Regulations. The inspectors confiscated the books and reported the matter to the police. Yesterday, the Jin Feng manager Chen Zhijun, the Zhen Changxiang manager Tang Liangui, the Hengxing manager Xu Hanchen, and the Da Shanghai manager Zhong Wenyu were summoned to the Summary Court of the Second Special District Court. Police Lawyer Fei Xizhen presented the case, and Liu Chunpu, the Stamp Tax Promotion Commissioner, claimed that the defendants had violated the Stamp Tax Law and requested severe punishment. The defendants confessed to forgetting to affix the stamps and requested leniency. Magistrate Ma Shounan fined Tang Liangui and Xu Hanchen 40 dollars each and Zhong Wenyu 30 dollars to serve as a warning.

Liu Qijing Comes to Shanghai to Practice Medicine

Mr. Liu Qijing, a medical graduate from Chiba, Japan, previously served his hometown, holding the position of Director of Ningbo Public Hospital for many years. He will surely benefit the poor and sick. It is also heard that Mr. Liu, with his remaining energy, concurrently serves as a professor at Southeast Medical College.

Readers' Letters

From Fangcao Shanren:

My father passed away early, and my mother was very strict. At the age of fourteen, I abandoned Chinese and English studies to learn the business of finance. I went from being an apprentice to managing money, from the silver room to the accounting room, from the accounting room to the street, and from the street to management (i.e., manager). Unexpectedly, in the first year of the Republic, the Wuchang Uprising occurred, and the store closed down, leaving me unemployed. Urged by my mother again, I entered the Hubei China Banking School, graduating after three years. Afterward, I spent more than ten years on the financial street in Hankou, but I could not find a way into the banking industry itself. This shows that studying is useless. Moreover, bank employees in Hankou are purely recommended by influential figures and have a shareholder nature, not those with academic research experience. Therefore, I gave up. Then, the split between Nanjing and Wuhan occurred, cash was frozen, and the store closed again, making me a second-time unemployed person. I returned to Huangshigang to engage in real estate or transportation business. Although the boat business has not succeeded, the real estate has indeed flourished. I built twenty-six buildings of civilian housing in Xuchunli, Huangshigang. Unexpectedly, I encountered an unprecedented and unmatched flood, all of which were washed away by the flood, leaving only stone, wood, and land. It is a sigh! This is my third unemployment recently. The pain I have suffered is unbearable. Fortunately, the water in the Yangtze River basin rises and falls with the autumn. The flood will recede soon. Moreover, Hankou is a famous commercial center in our country. The government will surely solve it with scientific methods in the future, so I will not discuss it for now. However, there are as many collapsed houses as in rural towns. Unfortunately, Hankou has no property companies, and it may be difficult to recover in the shortest period. Therefore, I borrow your newspaper to (1) introduce banking jobs, (2) have property companies in Shanghai set up branches in Hankou and I am willing to be a guide, (3) Shanghai people cooperate with Xuchun Property Joint Venture in Huangshigang, which is also very welcome. Our port is the location of various mines and forests in Daye, which is not only profitable but also very stable, and leaves a reputation for future generations. (4) Since abandoning the financial business four years ago, I have been engaged in the property industry and have quite a lot of knowledge about various projects. In the future, Hankou will need to scout engineering talents first. If there are large construction companies or factory construction companies in Shanghai, they can also provide preliminary effects. In short, I ask your newspaper to introduce the corresponding living conditions in the above four cities. Moreover, I have been reading your newspaper for thirty years and consider myself a loyal reader.

(Reply) Since you have specialized research, rich experience, and management skills, it is expected that you will get a chance shortly. We are answering publicly on the newspaper, as an aid to finding friends.

From Ms. Mou:

I am a female student who has just graduated from a famous university. For the sake of career issues, I have been running around for several days, but I only got anxiety and unemployment. Now I see the reply to Mr. Ye (the way out for college students) in the newspaper, which caused this letter. As you said, most of the college graduates nowadays study practical subjects very few, so that what they have studied is not what they can use, and they cannot cope with the needs of society. What I study is politics and economics, so there are many places where I am not suitable. But I am not disappointed because of this. I really want to find a reluctant way to find a way for myself, engage in writing and submitting articles, or translating books, but translating books is very difficult. As for writing articles, there are also many difficulties. Because one person's learning ability is limited, at this time of living alone in a foreign land, it is impossible to unite several comrades. After all, this layer must rely on one's own strength to do it. This is the first difficulty. I am a person who has rarely been in contact with society on weekdays and has no experience. I don't know what kind of articles to write and where to submit articles. This is the second difficulty. In terms of books, in addition to personal purchases, because the library is very far away, it is inconvenient to go back and forth, and it is not economical, so I can't get good books. This is the third difficulty. Other, what is called (short-term study of subjects that are more needed by society)? What kind of subjects are more needed and can be studied in a short period of time? Please tell me the details of the above items, so as to avoid difficulties. I also hope to continue to ask for advice in the future, it is very fortunate.

(Reply) We think that the three difficulties you mentioned are true. In the middle, you mentioned the article submission section, in addition to the whole book, various daily newspapers and famous weekly and monthly magazines all have the opportunity to contribute. You only need to try what you can do and like to do. However, the way of writing articles is all based on the usual specialized academic research and the observation of social conditions. You must accumulate deeply and richly, and then use appropriate art to develop it, so that it is a valuable work. If you write for the sake of writing, it is meaningless. Do you think this is right? Reading your letter, the writing is tactful, and the thinking is thorough. I believe that you have the ability to express your thoughts. I hope you will fight patiently and don't be discouraged. As for the short-term study of subjects, the Chinese Vocational Education Society attached to the Huanlong Road has several subjects. You may want to ask about it.

I am from Sanshui, Guangdong. I graduated from the high school department of St. John's University this summer. I am eighteen years old this year and I am determined to study fishery in order to prepare for the improvement and development of China's fishery industry. But I am suffering from the fact that there is no such school in China to study. Hebei Provincial Aquatic School, Tianjin, Junior College, Fishing and Manufacturing Department.

Fujian Private Jimei Senior Aquatic Navigation School, Xiamen, Senior Vocational Department, Fishing Department.

Liaoning Provincial Senior Aquatic Middle School, Yingkou, Senior Vocational Department, Fishing and Manufacturing Department.

Communication Stamp

Continued News of the Shenhu Steamer Damaging the Embankment

Yongan Steamer of the Yongan Bureau

The Shenjiao Steamer Has Also Suspended Service

The Yongan steamer within the Shenhu class, was detained by the Zhejiang Provincial Government because it damaged the Huzhou embankment, and fined 1.2 million yuan, which was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now I learned that the detained Yongan steamer belongs to the Yongan Steamer Bureau, not the Yongshun Company. After this incident, there was no solution for a while. Now I learned that the Huzhou County Government, in order to prevent further damage to the embankment, has set up watermarks to limit the size. If the inland steamers do not comply with the limited watermarks and run without authorization, in addition to immediately detaining the ships, they will be fined 600,000 yuan. After the promulgation of this serious ban, the Shanghai Steamer Bureaus have suspended the Huzhou class, and dare not violate this ban again.

The Shenjiao Steamer of the China Merchants Bureau has recently stopped sailing because the river water in the Zhujiajiao area has risen sharply and the county office has prohibited sailing.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The 101st Time

The 101st Inspection Report of the Issuing Reserve of the Central Bank says: According to Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this Council is responsible for inspecting the reserve for the issuance of exchange coupons of this Bank. The 101st inspection was held in the Issuing Bureau of this Bank on September 10, 20th year of the Republic of China. The total amount of exchange coupon reserve is 38,700,342 silver dollars, including cash reserve of 25,637,630 silver dollars. The cash reserve includes 16,908,276.61 silver dollars stored in the Bank's issuing treasury, 3,690,522 silver dollars stored in branches in various ports, and 5,038,831.39 silver dollars stored in the same industry. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 13,065,712 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold exchange coupons issued is 1 million yuan, and the total amount of customs gold exchange coupon reserve is 1 million yuan. The reserve includes 400,000 US dollars, stored in the same industry in this port. The fixed price is 40% customs gold. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Exchange Coupon Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The inspection results show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in line with the regulations. This report is hereby made. September 10, 20th year of the Republic of China. Ciyou Association Prevents Trafficking of Children

Strict Investigation at the Wharf and Railway Station

The flood this time has caused widespread disasters. The victims, supporting the old and carrying the young, came to Shanghai to take refuge, numbering in the thousands. Ignorant and profit-seeking traitors took the opportunity to buy the children of refugees and sell them as slaves, concubines, and prostitutes, which was also slightly heard. The Chinese Ciyou Association, with the purpose of protecting children's rights and seeking children's happiness, is deeply afraid that innocent disaster children will be abducted, deceived, and sold, falling into the endless hell. It has widely publicized it so that sympathetic people can report information for investigation. It is also strictly visiting at the wharf and railway station. If there are suspicious persons, they will be strictly interrogated. If there is evidence, they will be sent to the court for legal action. I hope sympathetic people will save the weak compatriots together.

Free Talk

Zhai Fu Talks About the Weeds in the Yard

The Commander-in-Chief of Five Cents

There are twenty-seven libraries in Tokyo, Japan. There are two large ones: one is the Tokyo Ueno Imperial Library; the other is the Tokyo Imperial University Library. The Ueno Library has 670,000 volumes. The Tokyo University Library has 600,000 volumes. Compared with the National Library of Paris with 5 million volumes, the British Museum Library of London with 5 million volumes, and the US Congressional Library in Washington with 4.4 million volumes, these two libraries are still a little less impressive, but in the culturally poor Orient, they can really be regarded as the best for a while. The Tokyo University Library was built with donations from the Rockefeller Foundation, founded by the American oil king, at a cost of 5.5 million Japanese yen, equivalent to 11 million Chinese yuan. The Rockefeller Foundation donated 4 million Japanese yen, and the remaining 1.5 million Japanese yen was paid by the national treasury. This library does not allow non-students to read. I got a letter of introduction from Ran Ansen of the Rockefeller Foundation, so I can find a way to go in to read, but because I was in a hurry to return to China, I did not get full use of it. The Ueno Library is open to the public, and anyone can go in to read for only five cents. The average number of readers per day is 1,200. If there are specialized questions, you can spend five cents to buy a research ticket to enter the research room to read. In this way, not only can you access the 670,000 volumes of books in the library, but the books outside the library can also be borrowed for you. This method can be regarded as extremely convenient for academic research. I told a friend this, and he said to me: (You spent five cents to become the commander-in-chief of this million-volume book, which is something to be proud of.)

The Weight of the Brain

— Hu Xingbo

The brain is the center of the nervous system. It controls all of our activities. For example, the movements of the five senses and hundreds of bones are all driven by the brain. According to physiological research, the more intelligent a person is, the heavier his brain is, and the more wrinkles on its surface. People cannot measure the weight of the brain and calculate the wrinkles of a living person, but only dissect and measure the dead.

According to research, the weight of a man's brain is greatest between the ages of fifty and sixty. The opposite is true for women. It is heaviest between the ages of twenty and thirty. Also, a man's brain is heavier than a woman's brain. The above survey is true in all countries of the world.

The brain weights of people of various races in the world are compared as follows.

European race male 1367 watts female 1206 watts. Malay Peninsula race male 1319 watts female 129 watts. American race (Indian) male 1308 watts female 1187 watts. Asian race male 2304 watts female 1194 watts. African race male 1293 watts female 1211 watts. Australian race male 1214 watts female 1111 watts.

The above is the average calculation of each race. Now, the weights of the brains of the great men of various countries are recorded as follows.

The brain of the great revolutionary Mr. Sun in our country. Its weight is very abnormal. According to the dissector, Mr. Sun's brain is actually one watt heavier than Lenin's in Russia. The weight of Mr. Sun's brain is 1505 watts, while Lenin's is 1504 watts.

The heaviest brain of the great men in the world. For the famous Russian writer Turgenev. Its weight is 2012 watts. The famous Prime Minister of Japan (end of the Meiji era) Taro Katsura was 1600 watts. The Japanese writer Natsume Soseki was 1425 watts. The European musical saint Chopin was more than 1420 watts. The above are recorded only after dissection after death. It is unknown whether there are those who have not been dissected or exceed the above records.

From the above, the superiority or inferiority of the human race seems to be innate rather than acquired. But that's not true. The weight of the brain is purely a matter of whether it is used or not. All things develop when used and degenerate when not used. Therefore, the weight of the brain and the number of wrinkles are purely a matter of the degree of use.

World Small Chronicle

An Educated Fish: At a certain university in Berlin, Germany, Professor De-Jing has attempted to teach fish how to read. The method used is to put their favorite food in bags marked with letters.

For example, the best food is marked with the letter A, and the second-best with the letter B. When the two bags are placed together, after some training, the fish will naturally find the A bag to eat. This shows that they have recognized the two letters A and B.

▲ The Inventor of the Tank: The most famous and effective weapon in killing the enemy during the European War, aside from poison gas, is the tank. It is said that it was initially proposed by a British officer, Lieutenant-Colonel E.D. Swinton, to the War Department of his country to rush the construction. After its creation, it was put into operation on the front lines. That was in October of 1914, and it achieved great results. However, recently, a certain German inventor claimed that he had drawn a tank design in 1913 and displayed it in Berlin. Therefore, the right to invention should belong to him. (Hai Ke)

Miscellaneous Talk on the Ksitigarbha Festival

— Bing Ding

The end of the seventh month of the abolished lunar calendar is commonly referred to as the Ksitigarbha Festival, which is also known as the birthday of Ksitigarbha Bodhisattva by Buddhists. Although the old calendar has been abolished, its profound influence on people's hearts over thousands of years cannot be eradicated immediately. It is traditionally believed that the seventh month is the Ghost Month, and families of modest means invariably hire monks to hold the Ullambana Festival to deliver the wandering souls. The wealthy families do even more.

According to folklore, Ksitigarbha's birthday falls on the 30th day of the intercalary seventh month. It is not the correct day if it is not an intercalary month or a short month. This saying is quite interesting. According to Buddhists, on this night, the Lord Ksitigarbha personally descends to hell to inquire about sufferings. At this time, the wronged souls are all delivered, and the gates of Fengdu City are opened to let them wander freely. Therefore, the Ullambana Festival is held to allow the wandering souls at the bottom of hell to enjoy the nectar and escape their sins. Although this matter belongs to superstition, the purpose of religion is mostly like this.

In the Suzhou area, on the day of the Ksitigarbha Festival, every household burns incense and candles at night, inserting them in the courtyard or placing them in front of the door. Wealthy families arrange them like stars, which is quite pleasing to the eye. This is called "Longing Incense." The initial purpose of this practice was to commemorate Zhang Shicheng of the early Ming Dynasty, so it was named "Longing." At that time, Shicheng defended Suzhou and was very popular with the people. The city was breached on the 30th day of the seventh month, and Shicheng died. The people of Suzhou mourned him, and thus the custom of "Longing Incense" arose, but they dared not speak of it openly. They only feigned lighting incense and candles to illuminate the path to the underworld. It is said that on this day, Fengdu opens its gates, and the wandering souls roam everywhere. Over time, the story was distorted, and the true meaning of the two characters "Longing" was gradually lost. People genuinely believe that it is held due to the Ksitigarbha Festival.

In the late Qing Dynasty, the Ullambana Festival on the day of the Ksitigarbha Festival was extremely lively, competing with events like the Three Kings Festival and the Zhou King Festival, or even surpassing them. In addition to the necessary programs such as stilt walking, platform performances, and tea box dances, there were also paper effigies of ghosts, such as Black and White Impermanence, Big Head and Small Head, Judges, Ox-Head and Horse-Face, etc., everything that one could imagine. When it was held, the streets were deserted, and its grandeur was unparalleled. Today, most of this has disappeared. Occasionally, one can see only a few gongs and drums and a few ghost effigies, and there is no interest to speak of. This kind of prototype of the Ullambana Festival can only be seen in Shanghai; in the inland, it has been suspended as a superstitious prohibition.

In Suzhou, on the night of the Ksitigarbha Festival, in addition to "Longing Incense," paper ingots are also burned outside the door. Later, every household did this, and beggars greatly benefited from it. Holding brooms and dustpans, they went from house to house sweeping up the ash and selling it to merchants. More than ten years ago, each person could get more than ten catties. Now, it is only a few catties. Therefore, beggars are overjoyed on the day of the Ksitigarbha Festival because they have unexpected income.

A Record of Bee's Help in Disaster Relief

— Yan Zi

There are many painting societies in Shanghai, but the Bee Painting Society, organized by famous painters Zheng Wuchang, Li Zuhan, Sun Xueni, Qian Shoutie, and others, has more than two hundred members, occupying a significant portion of the art world. Among the most famous members of the society are Xie Gongzhan, Zhang Shanzi, Ma Qizhou, He Tianjian, Xiong Songquan, Wang Shizi, Ye Weishen, Ma Wanli, Xie Zhiguang, Hu Ruosi, Ma Mengrong, and others, more than twenty in total. However, since Zheng Wuchang joined the army, the Bee Pictorial has also been discontinued. The society's affairs have been suspended in an invisible way. Last month, Zheng returned from the Eighth Army on leave, and Qian Shoutie also returned from Japan. The Bee Society held a banquet at Tao Le Chun to welcome Zheng and Qian and to discuss collecting paintings for disaster relief. At the table, Qian raised his glass to thank his colleagues and immediately proposed various methods for collecting paintings. Sun and Qian planned to underwrite the costs of opening a hotel and invite colleagues to cooperate for ten days. Zhu Rongzhuang believed that it would be a waste of money and that there might not be good works, so he asked everyone to sign up and commit to a certain number of paintings. Everyone agreed. On the spot, Xie Gongzhan, He Tianjian, Wang Shizi, Ma Mengrong, Qian Shoutie, Sun Xueni, Ye Weishen, Hu Ruosi, and others signed up for twenty paintings each. Ma Qizhou, Xiong Songquan, Zheng Wuchang, Zhu Rongzhuang, Gong Tiemei, Zhang Shanzi, and others signed up for ten paintings each. Li Zuhan, Shen Zicheng, and Xie Zhiguang signed up for five paintings each. Gu Ji signed up for ten paintings. All paintings were to be submitted within fifteen days. If there was spare time, they would collaborate at Chongfa Temple every evening to make up for any shortcomings. The motion was passed unanimously. By the time the banquet ended, the bell had already rung nine times.

Records of Things Seen and Heard in the Old Capital

— Zhu An

Tuancheng (Round City)

In previous years, when the emperor was in Xiyuan (West Garden), foreign envoys were required to have an audience at Chengguang Hall. The hall was built on top of Tuancheng. One would ascend through the side gate, level platform several acres in size, densely paved with patterned bricks. The hall was tall and imposing, with open windows and railings. Nearby, one could appreciate the waves of the North Sea; in the distance, the blue and green hues of the Western Hills floated. The exquisite palaces were truly the unique beauty of our country's architecture. According to its system, it has always existed in ancient times. Therefore, what is called "a platform to the right of the palace for emergencies" in ancient books. In modern times, the construction of platforms is rare. It must be that the Mongol Yuan did not master this skill. The scale of the palaces in Beijing all follows the old Yuan system. The emperors of the Ming Dynasty often held audiences on the platform. In the Qing Palace, only Tuancheng can be called a platform. If Yingtai is, it is not really a platform. I often worked here during the years of the Republic of China 12 and 13, enjoying its beautiful scenery morning and evening. I especially loved the ancient junipers in the courtyard. The junipers are characterized by white scales and bright green, with gnarled trunks and sparse shade. The leaves are similar to pine but slightly finer. Their posture is not as strange and outstanding as pine, but their elegance far surpasses it. Among them, the largest one is said to be a relic from the Jin Dynasty. More than ten younger ones are arranged next to it. Over the years, this place has been used as a public office. The ignorant servants used smoke and fire to fumigate it, and many have died, which is a pity. I once stroked and drew this tree and attached a poem to it, saying: "Eight hundred springs have passed before my eyes, and the palace trees on the precious platform are still jagged. How can the Jin Dynasty remember the peaceful times? The jade urn remains from after the calamity. It's useless to leave Qingyin to vulgar guests; if the waters of the return pool could wash away the dust. It should still regret growing old in the human world, not being used as firewood with the coiling dragon pillars." The jade urn in the poem refers to the wine urn made by Kublai Khan. During the Yuan Dynasty, it was always placed in the main hall during grand court assemblies. Later, it fell into the Zhenwu Temple outside Xihua Gate, and people called it the Jade Bowl Nunnery. In the tenth year of Qianlong, it was purchased for a thousand gold coins, moved to the courtyard of the hall, and covered with a stone pavilion, engraved with imperial poems and poems by various officials. The urn is made of black jade. According to its natural form, it is slightly carved. It can hold several stones of wine. This is truly a rare treasure of historical significance. As for the white jade Buddha enshrined in the hall, inlaid with precious stone璎珞, which ordinary people often admire endlessly, it is not enough to compare with this. People in the north do not know the two characters "juniper" and "cypress" and call it "white-bark pine." Looking at it for years, it seems to be covered with frost and snow. It can also be seen in suburban trips, and people in the south are often surprised by it as a wonder.

Rotary Club for Talking Novels

A Husband's Wife (11)

— Jiang Hongjiao

"You want to marry a thrifty and home-managing wife, why don't you marry Lanzhen! I married you for my husband to provide me with living expenses. Everything I use is necessary living expenses, and you feel the pain even for these. You might as well kill me, or divorce me, and I won't ask you for money anymore. If you have the ability, do it quickly! Otherwise, I am not Lanzhen. I won't cry, let alone commit suicide. You will suffer so much in your life. You are not worthy of being a man. You don't want to go to any social gatherings outside. You earn face for social gatherings outside, but you blame me with stinky words. I don't agree! You say, what ugly things did I do with Jingbo? I will confront Jingbo with you!" As she said, she really came to drag Mr. Chen. Mr. Chen was sitting on a small stool in a daze, trembling with anger. Unexpectedly, she dragged him with force, and he fell down. He still had some masculine spirit after all. He stood up, shook off his right arm, and pushed his wife. She didn't stand firmly and also fell to the ground. She stood up, knowing that she couldn't match a man in strength, so she could only use the things on the table to throw. Teapots, teacups, goldfish glass tanks, vases, cigarette dishes, everything was smashed.

(I only said one sentence, but you babbled a lot. Throwing things like this, what kind of decency is this! Give me some peace!)

(What is wrong with my peace that I have to be scolded by you? Give me proof. Insulting me like this, I will never let you off!)

They were arguing in the house, and Mr. Li could hear it. He walked over to knock on the door, wanting to persuade them, but he also heard Mr. Chen arguing, mentioning his name. Feeling guilty, he didn't dare to go. He knew that Mrs. Chen was very flexible and would never make a fuss about men coming home late at night, so he didn't sympathize much with Lanzhen, but Mr. Chen was feminine and secretly helped Lanzhen everywhere. The unrest in my family may have been caused by Mr. Chen saying bad things. The more Mr. Li thought about it, the more he hated Mr. Chen. But he had extraordinary admiration for Mrs. Chen.

To avoid disharmony in the family, he had to comfort his wife. He made up this reason and said to Lanzhen, "Listen! They are arguing, and things are being smashed. I wonder who is smashing them? Are you feeling better? Go and persuade them!"

"I have a headache and can't get up; you go!" Lanzhen had endured for a long time without saying a word, but now she spoke. Mr. Li knew that since she had spoken, it was a sign that she had calmed down, and he felt relieved.

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Market Trends in Disorder

▲ Gold Fluctuation: Yesterday, the 11th, the gold market situation was chaotic. The morning market recovered from weakness to strength, but the afternoon market tended to be sluggish, creating waves and appearing as rapid as lightning. A total of eight taels changed hands throughout the day. In the end, the price still rose by one tael, causing people to feel quite bewildered. The receipts and disbursements of the large firms were complicated, making it difficult to cope. As for the silver market, although it fell, it was not affected. It was probably due to Citibank making purchases, so the opening was low. However, foreign exchange became tight. Soon after, various parties were competing to buy, and it was heard that London silver bars seemed to be falling. The market received this news, and speculators eagerly bought in, causing the market sentiment to surge and break through the 770 tael mark. The afternoon market saw a reversal, probably due to the rumor that Bombay would expand the use of silver coins, causing a selling spree in the market and creating waves. Almost, the exchange rate also became loose and excessive. It is estimated that British gold rose from one shilling and three pence to three pence and one eight seven five, causing a sudden drop of more than seven taels to a little over sixty-three taels. Finally, it showed a slight peace. According to people in the industry, the current short selling may have to pay out, which is the opposite of the previous period, because the cash reserves are not abundant, and a certain bank may collect a huge number of 10,000 several thousand bars, which is forced by the short position, so the market price once rose, and the longs want to squeeze the shorts.

▲ Morning Market From Weak to Strong: At the opening of the October futures in the morning, it immediately fell by one tael and one qian to 763 taels and 8 qian. It is now estimated that 47 single palace silk factories and 6 double palace silk factories are operating in Shanghai. It is expected that the number will continue to increase in the coming days.

Large Batch of Japanese Tea Sold in Shanghai

Japanese green tea has recently been shipped in large quantities to Shanghai for sale. No Chinese merchants are willing to buy it. It is reported that the British firm Xiehe has purchased 5,000 boxes due to its low tea price, preparing to combine it with Chinese tea and ship it overseas for sale.

Youth Garden

Umbrella

— Wen Qing

In an island country where all four seasons feel like summer, the misty afternoon rain is like a poet's soul joyfully indulging in beautiful fantasies. Oiled paper umbrellas have become the beloved objects of those who are busy running around in life. Those merchants driven by money, during the more than three-month rainy season, also elaborately manufacture a very exquisite type of umbrella to supply to people's use. Even ordinary umbrellas are shiny and have three or four dazzling colors. Especially the umbrella of Miss Qiuyun, a student at the Xicheng Junior High School, is particularly exquisite and beautiful. It is said that her father bought it for her in a bustling capital city in Europe. Her school is very close to her home. She goes early and returns at noon, goes at noon and returns in the evening. Only during the afternoon rainy days of the more than three months is it annoyingly present. Every day she goes to school to attend classes, a beautiful umbrella follows her footsteps like her good friend. Since when, this beautiful umbrella has been deeply engraved in the heart of Mr. Zhang, the physics teacher.

That stubborn principal built a thick wall between the young teachers and the female students, forbidding male teachers from talking to female students except during classes. But one cannot blame that principal for being so strict, because the minds of those overseas Chinese students are too outdated. They still think like the 18th century and often talk about the story of Empress Dowager Cixi ruling from behind the curtain. But they still don't know what kind of person Empress Dowager Cixi actually was. Male teachers teaching female students are also considered traitors to the old ethics. They send their daughters to school to read Chinese books with trepidation, almost requiring the principal to write a guarantee to put in their hands before they feel at ease. People's mouths are inherently vicious. If a bit of gossip is blown into the ears of their parents, not only will the teacher's job be insecure, but the principal's position will also be fundamentally shaken. It was originally not easy to teach in the layers of oppression of the colonies. Once, the Dutch government inspected books and textbooks in a school, and found the two words "(revolution)" in a student's composition book, and arrested the teacher who corrected the composition and imprisoned him for three months before expelling him from the country. At the same time, in another school, a male teacher called a girl who was under twelve years old "(little sister)," and was also dismissed by the school board. Mr. Zhang was a little afraid of suffering the same misfortune, and kept the pain he had brought upon himself tightly hidden in the depths of his soul. His complexion became paler day by day, and he became thinner day by day. His colleagues even thought he was suffering from anemia and urged him to consult a doctor. I am afraid that there is no doctor in the world who would have such superb skills to cure him.

The owner of the umbrella, Miss Qiuyun's crystal-bead-like eyes, and her onion-like nose, were the raw materials that ignited the flames of love in Mr. Zhang's heart. He was originally a calm and composed young man, but he didn't know how the flames of love, which could not be extinguished by ocean water or seawater, were burning in his heart. Because of the harsh environment, he had no way to burst the flames in his heart. Therefore, distress, sorrow, worry, indifference, etc., all worked together to attack his weak soul, and a cruel longing mercilessly trampled on him. He had been unable to refuse his dreams many times. Sometimes he firmly rejected temptation, but temptation was stronger, and he was weaker than usual.

He originally did not like to smoke, but now he can often be seen releasing dense smoke from his nostrils. He wanted to turn his idleness and sorrow into green smoke and dissipate them into the boundless sky, but the smoke still circled around him. This long cloud of smoke seemed to shroud his gray fate, and he seemed to have no way to escape.

One afternoon, with heavy rain pouring down, he sat silently by the window, but who didn't know what he was thinking in his heart. In front of his dormitory were rows of dark green banana trees and coconut trees, their tears glistening, standing silently under the gloomy sky. His gazelle-like eyes, through the gaps in the coconut leaves, could see pedestrians on the road passing by in the heavy rain with umbrellas. He couldn't help but think of Miss Qiuyun's beautiful umbrella again. His lonely heart sank into a sad dream again. The sound of rain hitting banana leaves outside the window was like merciless cold bullets hitting his heart, causing him pain. His surroundings seemed to be filled with terrifying air, and his tears fell inexplicably like the sorrowful rain outside the window. He took out a white silk handkerchief from his pocket, gently wiped the tears from his cheeks, and lit another cigarette, because smoking was his only way to pass the time. Smoke filled the low and poorly lit room. He smoked and paced back and forth in the room, his eyes fixed on the ground. Undisciplined thoughts flowed backward in his brain like a raging flood. He lay down on the bed again, staring blankly at the white ceiling, lost in thought. Suddenly, a piece of unextinguished cigarette ash fell on his left cheek, burning a scar the size of a soybean, but he didn't seem to realize it. It is conceivable to what extent his nerves were deranged.

That day, when his class was over, he returned to his dormitory, lay on the bed, and rested his tired spirit. When a passionate fantasy was rushing through his mind, suddenly Miss Xi in the next room made a sound of calling her servant.

(Renna, Renna, quickly take Miss Qiuyun's umbrella to school. I just borrowed it. Hurry up, she's going home!)

When he heard the shadow of this voice containing Qiuyun's beautiful name, he immediately jumped out of bed and ran out of the door, three steps at a time. He saw that the beautiful umbrella was already in the hands of that rude servant. He rushed to the door and shouted,

(Renna, Renna, I'm going to the school. I'll take the umbrella for you!)

(No, this is Miss Qiuyun's umbrella. Mr. Xi wants me to take it over.)

(I know, I'll give it to her for you.)

He took the umbrella and held it tightly in his hand, as if he was holding his own life. After he walked out of the door, he realized that he was only wearing a white shirt and shorts. He usually loved to be handsome, but at this time he didn't care about anything, just rushing towards the school. His gazelle-like eyes glanced around the school, but he did not see Miss Qiuyun's figure in his eyes. Immediately, a sense of disappointment tightened his eyebrows. He simply placed the lovely umbrella lightly in the corner of the office, and ran to the window to look out. It turned out that Miss Qiuyun was still buried in her work, working on a composition in the classroom. At that time, a kind of inexplicable joy rose from his brain, eliminating the sorrow of disappointment without a trace. He stood outside like a puppet, waiting foolishly. He thought to himself, he wanted to take the opportunity of handing the umbrella to her to muster the courage to put the umbrella in her hand. He finally mustered the courage to walk up to her and gently asked her,

(Miss Wang, is your composition finished? So fast. Are you coming to school at four o'clock this afternoon?... Oh, this is your umbrella. Mr. Xi asked me to bring it over for you.)

(Thank you, sir.) She bowed, lowered her head, took her umbrella, and went home in the drizzle with her satchel. His disappointed eyes could only follow her slender figure.

Showing Off Skills

— Zhu Ziwei

On Saturday afternoon, a lot of people were crowding inside and outside the playground.

Yu was dressed more neatly than usual. He stood at the entrance of the playground, watching intently where people were coming from. The dark pupils in his black face sparkled, which would feel kind of cute and mysterious. Actually, mostly because they paid attention to Yu, everyone was crowding in front of the door, pointing and saying,

(Yu is going to do the high jump again today.)

The impression given was that deep. Everyone was there for him. Since a foot injury, he hadn't been seen practicing on this playground once. Even at the recent World Games, he hadn't prepared. Although he didn't think much of it, he still got a place at the World Games. He said that he unfortunately came in fourth because he was careless. Before the National Games, he was practicing on this playground. His friends thought he was working harder, wanting to see his performance earlier.

When Yu took off his coat and revealed a light blue vest and dark blue shorts, and exposed a pair of black and shiny arms and thighs, the muscles were bulging like a Roman general's idol. From a modern perspective, he had a dignified and healthy beauty. Really, I'm not being corny. The implication of the muscles was that of bravery. But there were also things that made you suspicious, suspicious that he couldn't compete with the huge foreigners. His short stature made it hard to believe that he could jump higher than foreigners.

When the high jump started, he was as light and agile as a swallow, as natural as a red carp jumping out of the water. The posture was graceful, and when he jumped, his body trembled, saying that he would rise even higher. After several jumps, he was on the slope, facing sideways, flying towards the center of the bamboo pole. When his body left the ground, his feet were turned back, higher than his head. You would worry about him, not to be nice, wouldn't he fall to his death? Miraculously, his feet passed the pole, and then they were turned upright again. As for the falling-to-death posture, people say that it's the earth's gravity, sucking up from the soles of the feet. I say, perhaps so.

The jumping enclosure was getting smaller and smaller, especially the children standing in the front row wanted to go forward to see more closely.

(Little brother, stand back a bit, let him jump higher so you can see,) Yu's friend Huang, he took care of the field, saying.

(Everyone look, hey, it's one meter seventy-five,) Cao, who was standing at the jumping stand, announced.

After the shout of "hey," it attracted everyone's attention. From Cao's line of sight, they turned to where Cao was looking. Strange, where did this miss come from, haven't seen her before. Like this, later on, the spectators were even busier. When they had a chance, they had to move their line of sight to look at her.

After passing one meter seventy-five, he didn't jump again afterwards.

After it dispersed, Yu wasn't seen.

Chen, nicknamed "Robber" in the ×× basketball team, said,

(Yu jumped high for her to see, to show off his skills.)

(Who is she?) someone asked.

(……)

(Oh, showing off his skills……) I said.

(Robber is speculating, Cao's report is also questionable,) I thought to myself on the way home, (Early autumn is full of the gentle meaning of spring, spring is like a dream, people need to change, really, early autumn is like spring.)

Shanghai Market

Business News

▲The Shanghai Guanghua Bookstore announced that from September 10th, the bookstore will hold a month-long autumn sale. The latest situation of the bookstore is as follows: (1) Since the revision of the new regulations of the Reading Club, the benefits obtained by members are even greater, and more people are joining. The deadline for recruitment is set for the end of October. Those who want to join must do so early. (2) In terms of publishing, Sinclair's masterpiece Boston, Student Enrollment Guidance, Student Reading Guidance, Zhang Ziping's long creation Flying Stars, Zhang Yiping's Youth Collection, etc. have all been published. (3) In terms of publications, the Reading Monthly is published, a special issue on literary research, and a small publication, Literary World, is published, with novel content. All members who join will still receive free copies as usual.

▲The Zhongxi Pharmacy announced that the Little Girl produced by this factory has the reputation of being the snowflake leader. It has not been released for long and is very popular. Since the beginning of autumn, orders from various foreign ports have been in short supply, and sales have increased rapidly. This product, once applied, makes the face tender and beautiful, hence the name Little Girl. Recently, this pharmacy recruited young girls as staff in the makeup department, which makes it even more colorful.

Social News

Life of Professional Women in New York

— Lin

Yasou was waiting for her in the hallway of a hotel. He was smart enough not to iron his clothes too flat every time she saw him. This afternoon, they talked freely, from the Dutch tunnels passing through the Hudson River to the latest dramas. Yasou still had no concept of worship. She felt attracted several times. Anyone who was colorful and good at fun could give her this feeling.

Yasou accompanied her back to the office. She had a magazine advertisement to be printed. The entire portion had been planned and drawn. All that was needed was for Maolin to write the manuscript. She had been thinking about this topic for several days. She knew to bring up the most prominent point, but she spent two hours of work to get this advertisement done. She handed it over to the publisher, who forwarded it to the printer. About two days later, Maolin wanted to read the first draft. At first, she looked at it alone, then she looked at it with the client to sort out the places that needed to be modified, and finally handed it over to the magazine for publication.

At half past four, Maolin decided to go home. She had a cup of tea on the way. After leaving the teahouse, she hired a street
